Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Tawfiq and Khidhlan as Divine Acts and Metaphorical Expression
Explanation of tawfiq/khidhlan as divine acts and metaphor justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tawfiq and khidhlan are entirely by Allah's will and power, and why the poet used metaphorical terms like 'arrival' and 'distance' for brevity.

Core Idea
Tawfiq and khidhlan are entirely from Allah, expressed through the metaphor of arrival and distance.

This passage from the poem clarifies a key point of Aqeedah: that both success (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan) are direct acts of Allah by His will and power. The poet uses a clever metaphor to express this concisely, and the commentator explains the reasoning behind this choice, addressing a potential misunderstanding about deviating from Quranic terminology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the translation. Notice how the commentator first states the doctrine, then explains the metaphor, then gives the logical consequence, then justifies the choice of words.
The passage is dense but logically ordered.
2
Understand the metaphor (kinaaya)
Focus on the statement: 'He used a metaphor of arrival for tawfiq and distance for khidhlan, expressing the necessary consequence (lazim) for the cause (malzum).' Think about how the effect (arrival at obedience) stands for the cause (tawfiq).
This is a common rhetorical device in Arabic.
3
Reflect on the rationale
Notice the last sentence: 'And he sufficed, by attributing the creation of tawfiq to Him, over attributing guidance (huda)...' This explains that the poet used tawfiq/khidhlan to avoid listing many Quranic terms, achieving brevity.
This prevents the misconception that the poet is changing the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن التوفيق والخذلان بمشيئته تعالى وقدرته، نصرته وإعانته. وهو المراد بقوله: (لمن أراد بعده عن رضاه ومحبته). فكنى عن التوفيق بالوصول، وعن الخذلان بالبعد، تعبيرا باللازم عن الملزوم. فالموفق لا يعصي؛ إذ لا قدرة له على المعصية، كما أن المخذول لا يطيع؛ إذ لا قدرة له على الطاعة. واستغنى بنسبة خلق التوفيق إليه تعالى عن نسبة الهداية، وبنسبة خلق الخذلان عن نسبة خلق الضلال.
An explanation that tawfiq and khidhlan are by His will and power, His help and assistance. And that is what is meant by His saying: 'for whomever He wills distance from His pleasure and love.' So he used the metaphor of arrival (wusul) for tawfiq, and distance (bu'd) for khidhlan, expressing the necessary consequence (lazim) for the cause (malzum). Thus the one granted tawfiq (muwaffaq) does not sin, because he has no power for sin; just as the one abandoned (makhdhul) does not obey, because he has no power for obedience. And he sufficed, by attributing the creation of tawfiq to Him, over attributing guidance (huda), and by attributing the creation of khidhlan over attributing the creation of misguidance (dalal).
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage explains that tawfiq and khidhlan are entirely by the will and power of Allah. It notes that the poet used the metaphor of 'arrival' (wusul) for tawfiq and 'distance' (bu'd) for khidhlan, which is a figure of speech where the necessary consequence (lazim) stands for the cause (malzum): since tawfiq leads to arrival at obedience and khidhlan leads to distance from it. The result is that the muwaffaq (one granted tawfiq) does not sin because he lacks the power to sin, while the makhdhul (one abandoned) does not obey because he lacks the power for obedience. The passage then answers a potential objection: why does the poet use tawfiq and khidhlan instead of the Quranic terms 'huda' (guidance) and 'dalal' (misguidance)? The reason is brevity (ikhtisar): by mentioning tawfiq, he dispenses with mentioning guidance, and by mentioning khidhlan, he dispenses with a longer list of terms like creation of misguidance, sealing, covering, etc.

Key Terms
موفق
مخذول
وصول
بعد
كنى
لازم
ملزوم
هداية
ضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The poet is deviating from the Quran by using terms like tawfiq and khidhlan instead of huda and dalal.
Correction: The poet is not changing the doctrine; he is using concise synonyms for brevity, as explained in the passage: 'And he sufficed, by attributing the creation of tawfiq to Him, over attributing guidance, and by attributing the creation of khidhlan over attributing the creation of misguidance.'

Checkpoint
Why did the poet use the terms 'arrival' (wusul) and 'distance' (bu'd) instead of directly saying tawfiq and khidhlan?
A) To emphasize that Allah guides and misguides.
B) To express the necessary consequence (lazim) instead of the cause (malzum) and to achieve brevity.
C) To avoid anthropomorphism.
D) To show that tawfiq and khidhlan are not real.

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq and khidhlan are entirely from Allah, and the poet uses the metaphor of arrival and distance to concisely express this, with the muwaffaq unable to sin and the makhdhul unable to obey.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself unable to commit a sin, do you immediately recognize that as Allah's tawfiq, or do you credit your own strength? How would your gratitude change if you truly believed you have no power to sin without His help?
?
In moments when you feel far from Allah and unable to worship, do you understand that as His khidhlan? Does that humble you to repent, or does it lead to despair? How should this lesson reshape your response to spiritual struggle?

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
Tawfiq and Khidhlan: Divine Acts and Their Effects
Sanusi defines tawfiq and khidhlan as divine acts and states their effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tawfiq (divine enabling) and khidhlan (abandonment) are acts of Allah's will and power, and that they directly determine a person's ability to obey or disobey.

Core Idea
Tawfiq and khidhlan are from Allah and define human capacity.

This lesson introduces the foundational concepts of tawfiq and khidhlan as used in kalam. The commentator begins by anchoring both terms in Allah's will and power, then draws out their direct effects: the enabled cannot sin, the abandoned cannot obey.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to see how the commentator opens with a declaration of divine will. Then read the translation.
Notice the use of parentheses for footnote markers.
2
Identify the two terms and their effects
The passage states that the divinely enabled does not disobey and the abandoned does not obey. Consider why this is so according to the text.
The reason given is that they lack the power for the opposite action.
3
Reflect on divine decree
Think about the implications for human free will. How does this align with the Ash'ari perspective on kasb (acquisition)?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن (1)، بيان أن التوفيق والخذلان بمشيئته تعالى وقدرته. نصرته وإعانته، وهو المراد بقوله: (لمن أراد بعده عن رضاه ومحبته؛ فكنى التوفيق المراد بالوصول، وعن الخذلان المراد بالبعد، تعبيرا باللازم عن الملزوم (1)؛ فالموفق لا يعصي؛ إذ لا قدرة له على المعصية(2)، كما أن المخذول لا يطيع؛ إذ لا قدرة له على الطاعة، واستغنى (3) بنسبة خلق التوفيق إليه تعالى عن نسبة الهداية، وبنسبة خلق الخذلان عن نسبة خلق الضلال . قوله: تعبيرا باللازم عن الملزوم أراد باللازم الوصول والبعد، والملزوم: التوفيق والخذلان. فالوصول لازم للتوفيق، والبعد لازم للخذلان. الشنواني. قوله: (فالموفق لا يعصي) أي: لا تقع منه معصية أصلا، بناء على أن الموفق يقابل الكافر والعاصي، أو لا يقع منه معصية الكفر؛ فيكون شاملا للعاصي، وحينئذ فيراد بالطاعة في تعريف التوفيق خصوص الإيمان، وكلام الشارح يقتضي الأول، وحينئذ فيقال: الموفق المخذول أعم من الكافر والعاصي، وقد جعل الشارح مقابلة المخذول الكافر، وترك العاصي فيقتضي أنه موفق، مع أن في كلام بعضهم ما يفيد أن المخذول يطلق على العاصي أيضا، ففي عبارة الشارح شيء؛ لأن أولها يقتضي أن المؤمن العاصي من قسم المخذول، وآخرها يقتضي قصر المخذول على الكافر، ولك أن تقول: لا يعصي من حيثية ما وفق فيه، والمخذول لا يطيع من حيث ما خذل فيه. وقد سئل الجنيد أيعصي الولي؟ فأطرق، ثم رفع رأسه وقال: {وكان أمر الله قدرا مقدورا} [الأحزاب: 38]. وقوله: (إذ لا قدرة له على المعصية) علة لقوله: (لا يعصي) فهو علة النفي لا المنفي. الشنواني. قوله (واستغنى) علته محذوفة، والأصل: استغنى عن هذه الأمور بلفظين لأجل الاختصار، وحاصله: إنه جواب عن سؤال مقدر تقديره: لم عدلت عما ورد به القرآن العزيز من إسناد الهداية والضلال إلى الله إلى التوفيق والخذلان؟ والجواب: إنما عدل للاختصار، بالنسبة للتعبير بالتوفيق وحده دون الهداية، والخذلان وحده دون ذكر خلق الضلال والختم والطبع والأكنة والمد في الطغيان، واحتاج لهذا لأن هذه الأشياء هي الواردة. الشنواني. قسم الإلهيات. والختم والطبع والأكنة والمد في الطغيان (1) قوله: (عن نسبة خلق (الضلال هو خلق القدرة على الكفر. وقوله: (والختم والطبع) هما كناية عن خلق الضلالة في العبد الذي هو الإضلال؛ فالإضلال والختم والطبع مترادفة، فالختم هو المشار إليه بقوله تعالى: {ختم الله على قلوبهم} [البقرة: 7] والطبع المشار إليه بقوله تعالى: {أولئك الذين طبع الله على قلوبهم} [النحل: 108] وقوله: (والأكنة) جمع كن بالكسر، وهو الستر، والمناسب أن يقول: وجعل الأكنة، وهو عبارة عن خلقها، والأكنة هي المشار إليها بقوله تعالى: {وجعلنا على قلوبهم أكنة أن يفقهوه} [الإسراء: 46] وقوله: (المد في الطغيان هو خلق الضلال مستمراً، وهو المشار إليه بقوله: {ويمدهم في طغيانهم يعمهون} [البقرة: 15] قال بعض المفسرين يمدهم: أي: يمهلهم في طغيانهم، أي: غلوهم في كفرهم يعمهون، حال، أي: يترددون. الشنواني. والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى: {إنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء} [القصص: 56]، {فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام ومن يرد أن يضله يجعل صدره ضيقا حرجا} [الأنعام: 125].
From (1), statement that divine enabling and abandonment are by His will and power. His help and assistance, and it is intended by His saying: (for whom He willed his distance from His pleasure and love; so He metaphorically expressed enabling intended by arrival, and abandonment intended by distance, expressing by the necessary for the necessary condition (1); so the divinely enabled does not disobey; since he has no power over disobedience (2), just as the abandoned does not obey; since he has no power over obedience, and He dispensed (3) by attributing the creation of enabling to Him, Exalted, over attributing guidance, and by attributing the creation of abandonment over attributing the creation of misguidance. His saying: expressing by the necessary for the necessary condition: he intended by the necessary arrival and distance, and the necessary condition: enabling and abandonment. So arrival is necessary for enabling, and distance is necessary for abandonment. Al-Shanwani. His saying: (so the divinely enabled does not disobey) i.e., no disobedience occurs from him at all, based on the view that the enabled is the opposite of the disbeliever and the disobedient, or no disobedience of disbelief occurs from him; so it includes the disobedient, and then obedience in the definition of enabling means specifically faith, and the commentator's words imply the first, and then it is said: the enabled and abandoned are more general than the disbeliever and the disobedient, and the commentator made the abandoned the opposite of the disbeliever, and left the disobedient implying he is enabled, though some scholars hold that the abandoned is also applied to the disobedient, so there is something in the commentator's expression; because its beginning implies that the believing disobedient is of the type of the abandoned, and its end implies restricting the abandoned to the disbeliever, but you may say: he does not disobey from the perspective of what he is enabled in, and the abandoned does not obey from the perspective of what he is abandoned in. Al-Junayd was asked: does a saint disobey? He bowed his head, then raised it and said: {And the command of Allah is a decree decreed} [al-Ahzab: 38]. And his saying: (since he has no power over disobedience) is a reason for his saying: (does not disobey), so it is a reason for the negation, not the negated. Al-Shanwani. His saying (He dispensed): its cause is omitted, and the original is: He dispensed with these matters by two expressions for the sake of brevity, and its summary: it is an answer to a presumed question: why did you turn away from what the Noble Qur'an came with of attributing guidance and misguidance to Allah to enabling and abandonment? The answer: He only turned for brevity, regarding expression by enabling alone without guidance, and abandonment alone without mentioning the creation of misguidance, sealing, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression, and he needed this because these things are what are reported. Al-Shanwani. Section of Divine Matters. And sealing, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression (1) His saying: (attributing the creation of misguidance is the creation of power over disbelief. And his saying: (and sealing and stamping) are metaphors for creating misguidance in the servant which is leading astray; so leading astray, sealing, and stamping are synonymous, so sealing is that referred to by His saying: {Allah has set a seal upon their hearts} [al-Baqara: 7] and stamping is that referred to by His saying: {Those are they upon whose hearts Allah has set a stamp} [al-Nahl: 108] and his saying: (and covers) plural of 'kinn' (covering), and it is appropriate to say: and He placed covers, which is an expression of creating them, and the covers are those referred to by His saying: {And We have placed upon their hearts covers lest they understand it} [al-Isra: 46] and his saying: (prolongation in transgression is the continuous creation of misguidance, and it is that referred to by His saying: {And We prolong their transgression while they wander blindly} [al-Baqara: 15] some exegetes said: 'We prolong them' means We give them respite in their transgression, i.e., their excess in disbelief, while they wander blindly, a circumstantial clause, i.e., they hesitate. Al-Shanwani. And the basis for that is His saying: {Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills} [al-Qasas: 56], {So whoever Allah wills to guide, He opens his breast to Islam; and whoever He wills to lead astray, He makes his breast tight and constricted} [al-An'am: 125].
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the poet's lines about divine enabling (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan). The commentator begins by stating that both are by Allah's will and power. He explains that the phrase 'for whom He willed his distance' means distance from Allah's pleasure, and that the poet used 'arrival' (al-wusul) to allude to tawfiq, and 'distance' (al-bu'd) to allude to khidhlan, as a necessary consequence (lazim) standing for the necessitated condition (malzum). The commentator then clarifies that the divinely enabled cannot commit sin because he lacks the power for it, while the abandoned cannot obey because he lacks the power for obedience. He then addresses why the poet used the terms tawfiq and khidhlan instead of the Qur'anic terms hidayah (guidance) and dalal (misguidance), explaining that this is for brevity: tawfiq alone covers all forms of guidance, and khidhlan alone covers all forms of misguidance, including sealing of hearts, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression. The commentator provides extensive footnotes (from al-Shanwani and others) clarifying the wording, the logical relationships, and the precise meanings of the terms, including a discussion on whether a believing sinner can be considered 'enabled' or 'abandoned'. The passage concludes by citing two Qur'anic verses (al-Qasas 56 and al-An'am 125) that establish that guidance and misguidance are from Allah alone.

Key Terms
توفيق
خذلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawfiq and khidhlan are merely metaphorical terms for reward and punishment.
Correction: They refer to Allah's creation of ability or inability to obey, which directly affects human acts.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the direct effect of tawfiq?
A) The enabled cannot sin
B) The enabled always obeys
C) The enabled receives paradise
D) The enabled has free will

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq gives the ability to obey, khidhlan removes it—both are directly from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever reflect that your ability to commit that sin was a form of khidhlan from Allah? How does that awareness change your reaction to your own sin—do you rush to repentance with humility, or do you remain content?
?
Think of a time you felt strong in obedience. Did you recognize that the strength itself was a gift of tawfiq, not from yourself? How can you cultivate a heart that constantly thanks Allah for enabling even the smallest good deed?
?
If your very power to obey or disobey is in Allah’s hands every moment, how does that reshape the way you begin your day? What specific change would you make tomorrow morning to live in constant reliance on His tawfiq?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
3 min
The Logical Relationship: Arrival and Distance as Necessary Consequences
Al-Shanwani clarifies the lazim-malzum relation in the poet's expression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical relationship of lazim (necessary consequence) and malzum (necessitated condition) as applied to tawfiq and khidhlan.

Core Idea
Arrival is necessary for enabling; distance is necessary for abandonment.

The previous lesson introduced tawfiq and khidhlan. Now the commentator elaborates on the logical device used: the poet expressed tawfiq by 'arrival' and khidhlan by 'distance' because these are necessary outcomes. This lesson unpacks that relationship.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the Arabic and translation. This is a very concise note from al-Shanwani.
2
Identify lazim and malzum
Find which terms are called lazim (necessary) and which are malzum (necessitated condition).
Lazim: arrival and distance; malzum: enabling and abandonment.
3
Think of other examples
Consider other pairs of cause and effect in theology or daily life that fit this lazim-malzum relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وحده دون ذكر خلق الضلال والختم والطبع والأكنة والمد في الطغيان، واحتاج لهذا لأن هذه الأشياء هي الواردة. الشنواني. قسم الإلهيات. والختم والطبع والأكنة والمد في الطغيان (1) قوله: (عن نسبة خلق (الضلال هو ومن يرد أن يضله يجعل صدره ضيقا حرجا} [الأنعام: 125].
From (1), statement that divine enabling and abandonment are by His will and power. His help and assistance, and it is intended by His saying: (for whom He willed his distance from His pleasure and love; so He metaphorically expressed enabling intended by arrival, and abandonment intended by distance, expressing by the necessary for the necessary condition (1); so the divinely enabled does not disobey; since he has no power over disobedience (2), just as the abandoned does not obey; since he has no power over obedience, and He dispensed (3) by attributing the creation of enabling to Him, Exalted, over attributing guidance, and by attributing the creation of abandonment over attributing the creation of misguidance. His saying: expressing by the necessary for the necessary condition: he intended by the necessary arrival and distance, and the necessary condition: enabling and abandonment. So arrival is necessary for enabling, and distance is necessary for abandonment. Al-Shanwani. His saying: (so the divinely enabled does not disobey) i.e., no disobedience occurs from him at all, based on the view that the enabled is the opposite of the disbeliever and the disobedient, or no disobedience of disbelief occurs from him; so it includes the disobedient, and then obedience in the definition of enabling means specifically faith, and the commentator's words imply the first, and then it is said: the enabled and abandoned are more general than the disbeliever and the disobedient, and the commentator made the abandoned the opposite of the disbeliever, and left the disobedient implying he is enabled, though some scholars hold that the abandoned is also applied to the disobedient, so there is something in the commentator's expression; because its beginning implies that the believing disobedient is of the type of the abandoned, and its end implies restricting the abandoned to the disbeliever, but you may say: he does not disobey from the perspective of what he is enabled in, and the abandoned does not obey from the perspective of what he is abandoned in. Al-Junayd was asked: does a saint disobey? He bowed his head, then raised it and said: {And the command of Allah is a decree decreed} [al-Ahzab: 38]. And his saying: (since he has no power over disobedience) is a reason for his saying: (does not disobey), so it is a reason for the negation, not the negated. Al-Shanwani. His saying (He dispensed): its cause is omitted, and the original is: He dispensed with these matters by two expressions for the sake of brevity, and its summary: it is an answer to a presumed question: why did you turn away from what the Noble Qur'an came with of attributing guidance and misguidance to Allah to enabling and abandonment? The answer: He only turned for brevity, regarding expression by enabling alone without guidance, and abandonment alone without mentioning the creation of misguidance, sealing, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression, and he needed this because these things are what are reported. Al-Shanwani. Section of Divine Matters. And sealing, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression (1) His saying: (attributing the creation of misguidance is the creation of power over disbelief. And his saying: (and sealing and stamping) are metaphors for creating misguidance in the servant which is leading astray; so leading astray, sealing, and stamping are synonymous, so sealing is that referred to by His saying: {Allah has set a seal upon their hearts} [al-Baqara: 7] and stamping is that referred to by His saying: {Those are they upon whose hearts Allah has set a stamp} [al-Nahl: 108] and his saying: (and covers) plural of 'kinn' (covering), and it is appropriate to say: and He placed covers, which is an expression of creating them, and the covers are those referred to by His saying: {And We have placed upon their hearts covers lest they understand it} [al-Isra: 46] and his saying: (prolongation in transgression is the continuous creation of misguidance, and it is that referred to by His saying: {And We prolong their transgression while they wander blindly} [al-Baqara: 15] some exegetes said: 'We prolong them' means We give them respite in their transgression, i.e., their excess in disbelief, while they wander blindly, a circumstantial clause, i.e., they hesitate. Al-Shanwani. And the basis for that is His saying: {Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills} [al-Qasas: 56], {So whoever Allah wills to guide, He opens his breast to Islam; and whoever He wills to lead astray, He makes his breast tight and constricted} [al-An'am: 125].
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the poet's lines about divine enabling (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan). The commentator begins by stating that both are by Allah's will and power. He explains that the phrase 'for whom He willed his distance' means distance from Allah's pleasure, and that the poet used 'arrival' (al-wusul) to allude to tawfiq, and 'distance' (al-bu'd) to allude to khidhlan, as a necessary consequence (lazim) standing for the necessitated condition (malzum). The commentator then clarifies that the divinely enabled cannot commit sin because he lacks the power for it, while the abandoned cannot obey because he lacks the power for obedience. He then addresses why the poet used the terms tawfiq and khidhlan instead of the Qur'anic terms hidayah (guidance) and dalal (misguidance), explaining that this is for brevity: tawfiq alone covers all forms of guidance, and khidhlan alone covers all forms of misguidance, including sealing of hearts, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression. The commentator provides extensive footnotes (from al-Shanwani and others) clarifying the wording, the logical relationships, and the precise meanings of the terms, including a discussion on whether a believing sinner can be considered 'enabled' or 'abandoned'. The passage concludes by citing two Qur'anic verses (al-Qasas 56 and al-An'am 125) that establish that guidance and misguidance are from Allah alone.

Key Terms
اللازم
الملزوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Shanwani, what is the malzum for 'arrival'?
A) Distance
B) Tawfiq
C) Khidhlan
D) Guidance

Key Takeaway
The poet uses arrival and distance as necessary consequences to refer to tawfiq and khidhlan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself distant from obedience, do you recognize that as a necessary consequence of Allah's abandonment (khidhlan)? What does that reveal about your own efforts and reliance on Him?
?
If arrival at goodness is only a consequence of divine tawfiq, not your own doing, does your heart feel genuine humility before Allah, or do you secretly attribute your successes to yourself?
?
Are you more concerned with the outward signs of arrival (like feeling close to Allah) or with seeking the enabling itself? Which does your du'a and daily struggle reflect?

Justification for Using Tawfiq and Khidhlan Instead of Hidayah and Dalal
Al-Shanwani provides the reason for the poet's choice and lists Qur'anic equivalents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the poet chose the terms tawfiq and khidhlan over the Qur'anic terms hidayah and dalal, and how they concisely encompass all related divine acts.

Core Idea
Tawfiq and khidhlan are concise synonyms that cover all Qur'anic expressions of guidance and misguidance.

A potential question arises: why not use the direct Qur'anic terms? The commentator explains that the poet adopted tawfiq and khidhlan for brevity, as one term can replace multiple Qur'anic expressions like sealing, stamping, and covers. This lesson presents that justification and lists the scriptural equivalents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the presumed question and the answer given.
2
Identify the list of Qur'anic terms
The passage mentions sealing (khatm), stamping (tab'), covers (akinnah), and prolongation in transgression (madd fi al-tughyan). Find their definitions.
3
Connect to supporting verses
Each term is linked to a specific Qur'anic verse. Look up those verses to see the context.

عن (1)، بيان أن التوفيق والخذلان بمشيئته تعالى وقدرته. نصرته وإعانته، وهو المراد بقوله: (لمن أراد بعده عن رضاه ومحبته؛ فكنى التوفيق المراد بالوصول، وعن الخذلان المراد بالبعد، تعبيرا باللازم عن الملزوم (1)؛ فالموفق لا يعصي؛ إذ لا قدرة له على المعصية(2)، كما أن المخذول لا يطيع؛ إذ لا قدرة له على الطاعة، واستغنى (3) بنسبة خلق التوفيق إليه تعالى عن نسبة الهداية، وبنسبة خلق الخذلان عن نسبة خلق الضلال . قوله: تعبيرا باللازم عن الملزوم أراد باللازم الوصول والبعد، والملزوم: التوفيق والخذلان. فالوصول لازم للتوفيق، والبعد لازم للخذلان. الشنواني. قوله: (فالموفق لا يعصي) أي: لا تقع منه معصية أصلا، بناء على أن الموفق يقابل الكافر والعاصي، أو لا يقع منه معصية الكفر؛ فيكون شاملا للعاصي، وحينئذ فيراد بالطاعة في تعريف التوفيق خصوص الإيمان، وكلام الشارح يقتضي الأول، وحينئذ فيقال: الموفق المخذول أعم من الكافر والعاصي، وقد جعل الشارح مقابلة المخذول الكافر، وترك العاصي فيقتضي أنه موفق، مع أن في كلام بعضهم ما يفيد أن المخذول يطلق على العاصي أيضا، ففي عبارة الشارح شيء؛ لأن أولها يقتضي أن المؤمن العاصي من قسم مقدورا} [الأحزاب: 38]. وقوله: (إذ لا قدرة له على المعصية) علة لقوله: (لا يعصي) فهو علة النفي لا المنفي. الشنواني. قوله (واستغنى) علته محذوفة، والأصل: استغنى عن هذه الأمور بلفظين لأجل الاختصار، وحاصله: إنه جواب عن سؤال مقدر تقديره: لم عدلت عما ورد به القرآن العزيز من إسناد الهداية والضلال إلى الله إلى التوفيق والخذلان؟ والجواب: إنما عدل للاختصار، بالنسبة للتعبير بالتوفيق وحده دون الهداية، والخذلان وحده دون ذكر خلق الضلال والختم والطبع والأكنة والمد في الطغيان، واحتاج لهذا لأن هذه الأشياء هي الواردة. الشنواني. قسم الإلهيات. والختم والطبع والأكنة والمد في الطغيان (1) قوله: (عن نسبة خلق (الضلال هو Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the poet's lines about divine enabling (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan). The commentator begins by stating that both are by Allah's will and power. He explains that the phrase 'for whom He willed his distance' means distance from Allah's pleasure, and that the poet used 'arrival' (al-wusul) to allude to tawfiq, and 'distance' (al-bu'd) to allude to khidhlan, as a necessary consequence (lazim) standing for the necessitated condition (malzum). The commentator then clarifies that the divinely enabled cannot commit sin because he lacks the power for it, while the abandoned cannot obey because he lacks the power for obedience. He then addresses why the poet used the terms tawfiq and khidhlan instead of the Qur'anic terms hidayah (guidance) and dalal (misguidance), explaining that this is for brevity: tawfiq alone covers all forms of guidance, and khidhlan alone covers all forms of misguidance, including sealing of hearts, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression. The commentator provides extensive footnotes (from al-Shanwani and others) clarifying the wording, the logical relationships, and the precise meanings of the terms, including a discussion on whether a believing sinner can be considered 'enabled' or 'abandoned'. The passage concludes by citing two Qur'anic verses (al-Qasas 56 and al-An'am 125) that establish that guidance and misguidance are from Allah alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The poet changed the meaning by using different terms.
Correction: The terms are concise synonyms; they do not change the doctrine.

A) To avoid theological controversy
B) For brevity
C) To emphasize human free will

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq and khidhlan are concise terms that summarize all Qur'anic descriptions of divine guidance and misguidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly recognize that every moment of faith and obedience in your life is a gift of tawfiq from Allah, not your own doing? How does this realization humble you, and what can you do today to acknowledge His enablement?
?
When you read about Allah sealing hearts and prolonging transgression, does it stir fear in your soul? Are there areas of sin you are persisting in that might be a sign of khidhlan? What concrete step will you take to seek His guidance before it is too late?
?
If guidance and misguidance are entirely from Allah, have you thanked Him sincerely for guiding you to Islam while others are astray? Or do you look down on the misguided, forgetting that without His tawfiq, you would be in the same state? How will you show gratitude today?

The Case of the Sinning Believer: Is He Enabled or Abandoned?
Al-Shanwani analyzes the statement 'the enabled does not disobey' and addresses the case of the sinning believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate about whether a believing sinner is considered divinely enabled (tawfiq) or abandoned (khidhlan), and the nuanced resolution that a person may be enabled in some respects and abandoned in others.

Core Idea
A believer may be enabled in some respects and abandoned in others.

This lesson delves into a nuanced discussion: if tawfiq means one cannot sin, how do we account for believers who sin? The commentator presents different interpretations and the story of Junayd al-Baghdadi, highlighting the complexity of divine decree and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two interpretations of 'the enabled does not disobey'.
2
Understand the apparent contradiction
The text seems to both include and exclude the sinning believer from abandonment. Find where this occurs.
3
Reflect on Junayd's answer
When asked if a saint can sin, Junayd quotes a verse about divine decree. What does this imply about human actions?

يمهلهم في طغيانهم، أي: غلوهم في كفرهم يعمهون، حال، أي: يترددون. الشنواني. والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى: {إنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء} [القصص: 56]، {فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام ومن يرد أن يضله يجعل صدره ضيقا حرجا} [الأنعام: 125].
From (1), statement that divine enabling and abandonment are by His will and power. His help and assistance, and it is intended by His saying: (for whom He willed his distance from His pleasure and love; so He metaphorically expressed enabling intended by arrival, and abandonment intended by distance, expressing by the necessary for the necessary condition (1); so the divinely enabled does not disobey; since he has no power over disobedience (2), just as the abandoned does not obey; since he has no power over obedience, and He dispensed (3) by attributing the creation of enabling to Him, Exalted, over attributing guidance, and by attributing the creation of abandonment over attributing the creation of misguidance. His saying: expressing by the necessary for the necessary condition: he intended by the necessary arrival and distance, and the necessary condition: enabling and abandonment. So arrival is necessary for enabling, and distance is necessary for abandonment. Al-Shanwani. His saying: (so the divinely enabled does not disobey) i.e., no disobedience occurs from him at all, based on the view that the enabled is the opposite of the disbeliever and the disobedient, or no disobedience of disbelief occurs from him; so it includes the disobedient, and then obedience in the definition of enabling means specifically faith, and the commentator's words imply the first, and then it is said: the enabled and abandoned are more general than the disbeliever and the disobedient, and the commentator made the abandoned the opposite of the disbeliever, and left the disobedient implying he is enabled, though some scholars hold that the abandoned is also applied to the disobedient, so there is something in the commentator's expression; because its beginning implies that the believing disobedient is of the type of the abandoned, and its end implies restricting the abandoned to the disbeliever, but you may say: he does not disobey from the perspective of what he is enabled in, and the abandoned does not obey from the perspective of what he is abandoned in. Al-Junayd was asked: does a saint disobey? He bowed his head, then raised it and said: {And the command of Allah is a decree decreed} [al-Ahzab: 38]. And his saying: (since he has no power over disobedience) is a reason for his saying: (does not disobey), so it is a reason for the negation, not the negated. Al-Shanwani. His saying (He dispensed): its cause is omitted, and the original is: He dispensed with these matters by two expressions for the sake of brevity, and its summary: it is an answer to a presumed question: why did you turn away from what the Noble Qur'an came with of attributing guidance and misguidance to Allah to enabling and abandonment? The answer: He only turned for brevity, regarding expression by enabling alone without guidance, and abandonment alone without mentioning the creation of misguidance, sealing, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression, and he needed this because these things are what are reported. Al-Shanwani. Section of Divine Matters. And sealing, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression (1) His saying: (attributing the creation of misguidance is the creation of power over disbelief. And his saying: (and sealing and stamping) are metaphors for creating misguidance in the servant which is leading astray; so leading astray, sealing, and stamping are synonymous, so sealing is that referred to by His saying: {Allah has set a seal upon their hearts} [al-Baqara: 7] and stamping is that referred to by His saying: {Those are they upon whose hearts Allah has set a stamp} [al-Nahl: 108] and his saying: (and covers) plural of 'kinn' (covering), and it is appropriate to say: and He placed covers, which is an expression of creating them, and the covers are those referred to by His saying: {And We have placed upon their hearts covers lest they understand it} [al-Isra: 46] and his saying: (prolongation in transgression is the continuous creation of misguidance, and it is that referred to by His saying: {And We prolong their transgression while they wander blindly} [al-Baqara: 15] some exegetes said: 'We prolong them' means We give them respite in their transgression, i.e., their excess in disbelief, while they wander blindly, a circumstantial clause, i.e., they hesitate. Al-Shanwani. And the basis for that is His saying: {Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills} [al-Qasas: 56], {So whoever Allah wills to guide, He opens his breast to Islam; and whoever He wills to lead astray, He makes his breast tight and constricted} [al-An'am: 125].
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the poet's lines about divine enabling (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan). The commentator begins by stating that both are by Allah's will and power. He explains that the phrase 'for whom He willed his distance' means distance from Allah's pleasure, and that the poet used 'arrival' (al-wusul) to allude to tawfiq, and 'distance' (al-bu'd) to allude to khidhlan, as a necessary consequence (lazim) standing for the necessitated condition (malzum). The commentator then clarifies that the divinely enabled cannot commit sin because he lacks the power for it, while the abandoned cannot obey because he lacks the power for obedience. He then addresses why the poet used the terms tawfiq and khidhlan instead of the Qur'anic terms hidayah (guidance) and dalal (misguidance), explaining that this is for brevity: tawfiq alone covers all forms of guidance, and khidhlan alone covers all forms of misguidance, including sealing of hearts, stamping, covers, and prolongation in transgression. The commentator provides extensive footnotes (from al-Shanwani and others) clarifying the wording, the logical relationships, and the precise meanings of the terms, including a discussion on whether a believing sinner can be considered 'enabled' or 'abandoned'. The passage concludes by citing two Qur'anic verses (al-Qasas 56 and al-An'am 125) that establish that guidance and misguidance are from Allah alone.

Key Terms
الموفق
المخذول
الولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A believer cannot sin at all if he is divinely enabled.
Correction: Tawfiq may be specific to certain actions; a believer can sin in some respects while being enabled in faith.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the apparent contradiction about the sinning believer?
A) By saying the believer is always enabled
B) By saying the believer is always abandoned
C) By distinguishing between different respects of enabling/abandonment
D) By denying that believers sin

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq and khidhlan are not absolute categories; they can apply to the same person in different respects, reflecting the complexity of divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own life, in which specific areas do you feel most 'abandoned' by Allah in terms of struggling with sin? How does this lesson's distinction between being enabled in some respects and abandoned in others change the way you view your efforts and your dua?
?
Al-Junayd simply quoted 'And the command of Allah is a decree decreed' when asked if a saint can sin. Is there a sin in your life that you have not fully accepted as part of Allah's decree? How would genuinely believing that it was decreed affect your repentance and your relationship with Allah?
?
The lesson says that a believer can be both enabled and abandoned. Think of a time you disobeyed despite knowing better. Did you feel enabled in your faith but abandoned in that moment? What does that teach you about your dependence on Allah's tawfiq in every action?

The Ash'ari Position on Threat (al-Wa'id)
Sanusi presents the Ash'ari view on divine threat with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari view that God's threat of punishment is not absolute; He may forgive, and why breaking a threat is considered generosity rather than deficiency.

Core Idea
God's threatening is not a promise—breaking a threat is generosity, not deficiency.

Sanusi now turns to the controversial topic of divine threat (al-wa'id). The Ash'aris argue that God's threat to punish sinners is not absolute; He may choose to forgive. This lesson presents their scriptural and rational proofs, showing how human customs about threats and promises shed light on God's actions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of wa'id
Read the passage's first sentence defining wa'id as Allah's punishment of disbelievers and sinners. This sets the stage for the debate.
Wa'id is distinct from wa'd (promise).
2
Identify the Ash'ari position
Notice that the Ash'aris hold it permissible for Allah to forgive sins and not punish, and equally permissible to punish. This is the core claim.
3
Examine the Qur'anic evidence
Two verses are cited: one general (''Indeed Allah forgives all sins'') and one on Jesus' tongue showing forgiveness is possible. Reflect on why these support the Ash'ari view.
The second verse implies that Jesus knew forgiveness was possible.
4
Analyze the rational argument from custom
Sanusi argues that among humans, breaking a threat is considered generosity, while breaking a promise is a deficiency. Since Allah is perfect, He can break a threat but not a promise.
The poet's line illustrates this human custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوعيد ـ وهو تعذيب الله الكفار والعصاة وإدخالهم النَّار - فذهب الأشاعرة إلى أنه يجوز أنْ يغفر الله الذَّنوب ، ولا يدخل مرتكبها النَّار ولا يعذِّبه ، كما يجوز أن يعاقبه ويدخله النار ، واستدلوا على ذلك بنحو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ الله يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ جَمِيعًا [الزمر: ٥٣] ، وبقوله سبحانه على لسان عيسى : وإِن تُعَذِّبْهُمْ فَإِنَّهُمْ عِبَادُكَ وَإِن تَغْفِرْ لَهُمْ فَإنَّكَ أَنتَ الْعَزِيزُ الْحَكِيمُ﴾ [المائدة: ۱۱۸] ولولا أن عيسى يعلم أنَّ غُفران الذُّنوبِ جائز شرعاً لما قال هذا، وأيضاً فإن إخلاف الإنسانِ ما توعد به وهدد به لا يُعدُّ نقصاً ، بل يُعدُّ كَرَماً وحُسنَ خُلُقٍ ، وقد تمدح به النَّاس ؛ فمن ذلك قول الشاعر:
وَإِنِّي وَإِنْ أَوْعَدْتُهُ أَوْ وَعَدْتُهُ لَمُخْلِفُ إِيعَادِي وَمُنْجِزُ مَوْعِدِي فلما اختلفَ أمرُ الخُلف في الوعد والوعيد ، فعدَّ العقلاء إخلاف الوعد نقصا، وعدوا إخلاف الوعيد كَرَما ، ولما كان الله الله موصوفا بكلّ كمال، جاز أنْ يُخلِفَ الإيعاد، ولم يجز أنْ يُخلف الوعد.
As for the threat—and it is Allah's punishing the disbelievers and sinners and entering them into the Fire—the Ash'aris held that it is permissible for Allah to forgive sins, and not enter the committer into the Fire nor punish him, just as it is permissible for Him to punish him and enter him into the Fire. And they adduced as evidence His saying the Exalted: {Indeed Allah forgives all sins} [Az-Zumar: 53], and His saying the Glorified upon the tongue of Jesus: {If You punish them, indeed they are Your servants; and if You forgive them, indeed You are the Mighty, the Wise} [Al-Ma'idah: 118]. And were it not that Jesus knew that the forgiveness of sins is legally permissible, he would not have said this. Also, a person's breaking what he has threatened and warned with is not considered a deficiency, but rather it is considered generosity and good character, and people have been praised for it. Among that is the saying of the poet: 'And indeed, if I threaten him or promise him, I am one who breaks my threat and fulfills my promise.' Thus, since the matter of breaking differs between promise and threat—the intelligent consider breaking a promise a deficiency, and they consider breaking a threat generosity—and since Allah is described with all perfection, it is permissible for Him to break the threat, and it is not permissible for Him to break the promise.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari position on al-wa'id (threat). The author first defines threat as Allah's punishment of disbelievers and sinners and entering them into the Fire. The Ash'aris hold that it is permissible for Allah to forgive sins and not punish the sinner, just as it is permissible for Him to punish. They use two Qur'anic proofs: first, the verse 'Indeed Allah forgives all sins' (Az-Zumar: 53), which is general; second, the verse on Jesus' tongue in Al-Ma'idah: Jesus says that if Allah punishes them they are His servants, and if He forgives them He is Mighty and Wise—showing that Jesus considered forgiveness a possibility, otherwise he would not have said it. Then the author adds a rational argument: breaking a threat by a human is not considered a deficiency; rather it is generosity and good character, and people are praised for it. He quotes a poet saying he breaks his threat but fulfills his promise. Since intelligent people distinguish between breaking a promise (deficiency) and breaking a threat (generosity), and Allah possesses all perfection (free from deficiency), it is permissible for Him to break the threat but not the promise.

Key Terms
الوعيد
يغفر
يجوز
الإيعاد
الوعد
الكرامة
النقص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God must always carry out His threat, otherwise He would be a liar.
Correction: The Ash'aris show that breaking a threat is not a deficiency but an act of generosity, based on human custom and Allah's perfection. God is free to forgive.

Checkpoint
What is the Ash'ari position on the threat (al-wa'id)?
A) God must carry out the threat because He said so.
B) God may forgive and not punish, because threatening is conditional on will.
C) God always punishes the sinner to be just.
D) Threat is like promise and cannot be broken.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari view is that God may forgive sins, and breaking a threat is permissible because it is an act of generosity, not a deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that God may break His threat out of generosity, does that make you feel more hopeful or more complacent about your sins? Honestly examine your heart: are you banking on God's forgiveness to keep sinning, or does this knowledge move you to deeper gratitude and obedience?
?
You have likely threatened someone in anger. After this lesson, can you say you've ever broken a threat as an act of generosity? How does the human example of breaking threats for the sake of good character challenge you to forgive others when they deserve punishment?
?
If God's threat is not a binding promise, then His mercy is the final word. What sin are you holding onto because you think God's threat is absolute? Will you now turn to Him, trusting that His generosity outweighs His threat, and ask for forgiveness today?

The Mu'tazili Position on Threat and Their Arguments
Sanusi presents the Mu'tazili view that God cannot break threat, with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili argument that God cannot break His threat and the three corruptions that would follow if He did.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilis argue that breaking the threat would contradict God's truthfulness, justice, and eternal punishment.

The Mu'tazili school is known for its rationalist approach to theology. Here, Sanusi presents their argument that God cannot break His threat of punishment, any more than He can break His promise of reward. The Mu'tazilis support this with three consequence-based arguments, each showing that breaking the threat would lead to a contradiction in divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the overall claim and its supporting reasons.
Notice the use of 'لا يجوز' which indicates impossibility.
2
Identify the Mu'tazili claim
Find the opening statement about breaking threat and promise.
3
Examine the three corruptions
List each corruption and understand why the Mu'tazilis see them as impossible.
The first corruption involves lying, the second involves alteration of speech, the third involves denial of eternal punishment.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why the Mu'tazilis consider these consequences decisive.
This shows their commitment to God's justice and truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب المعتزلة إلى أنه لا يجوز عليه سبحانه أن يخلِفَ الوعيد كما لا يجوز عليه أن يُخلف الوعد.
واستدلوا على ذلك بأنَّه لو جاز تخلُّف الوعيد للزم عنه مفاسد كثيرة: منها: وقوع الكذب في خبره تعالى الذي أخبر فيه بأنه يعاقب من اقترف الآثام، والكذب في خبره تعالى محال .
ومنها: تبدلُ القول ، وهو يقول : مَا يُبَدَّلُ الْقَوْلُ لَدَى وَمَا أَنَا بِظَلَمِ لِلْعَبِيدِ ) [ق: ٢٩].
ومنها: أنه يستتبع القول بعدم خلودِ الكُفار في النَّار ؛ حيث جوزنا أن يعفو الله ، وخلود الكفار في النَّار مما قامت الأدلة المتوافرة عليه .
And the Mu'tazilis held that it is not permissible for Him the Glorified to break the threat, just as it is not permissible for Him to break the promise. And they adduced for that that if breaking of the threat were permissible, many corruptions would follow from it: among them: occurrence of lying in His report the Exalted in which He informed that He will punish whoever commits sins, and lying in His report the Exalted is impossible. And among them: alteration of speech, while He says: {My word is not changed, and I am not unjust to the servants} [Qaf: 29]. And among them: that it entails the saying that disbelievers are not eternally in the Fire, since we allowed that Allah may forgive, while the eternal punishment of disbelievers in the Fire is something upon which abundant proofs have been established.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazili position on threat and their three arguments. The Mu'tazilis assert that it is not permissible for God to break the threat, just as it is not permissible to break the promise. They argue that if breaking the threat were permissible, three corruptions would follow: (1) It would entail lying in God's report that He will punish sinners—God's report cannot be false. (2) It would entail alteration of speech, contradicting the verse 'My word is not changed'. (3) It would lead to denying the eternal punishment of disbelievers, since if forgiveness is possible, eternal punishment might not occur, but abundant proofs have established their eternal damnation. The Mu'tazilis thus see breaking the threat as inconsistent with divine attributes.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
يخلِف
الوعيد
الكذب
تبدل القول
الخلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazilis deny all forgiveness entirely.
Correction: They argue that threat cannot be broken, but they do allow forgiveness in some cases, as indicated by the phrase 'since we allowed that Allah may forgive' in the passage.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilis, what would follow if it were permissible for God to break the threat?
A) It would show God's generosity.
B) It would entail lying, alteration of speech, and denial of eternal punishment.
C) It would make God forgetful.
D) Nothing; it is already permissible.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilis argue that God's threat of punishment is as binding as His promise, because breaking it would entail lying, change in His word, and denial of eternal punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if God's threat is not serious, assuming He will overlook your sins? How does the Mu'tazili insistence that the threat cannot be broken change your view of divine accountability? What would you have to do differently today if you truly believed every threat in the Quran is binding?
?
The Mu'tazilis argue that breaking the threat would imply a change in God's word. When you read verses about punishment, do you trust that they will be fulfilled exactly? Is there a point where you hope they are just 'warnings'? Where does that leave your relationship with God's truthfulness?
?
If God's threat is as certain as His promise, how does that affect the urgency of your repentance? Are you waiting for a 'maybe' or are you responding to a definite decree? What would it mean to live today with the full weight of that certainty?

Ash'ari Responses to Mu'tazili Objections on Threat
Sanusi enumerates three Ash'ari replies to Mu'tazili objections about threat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three Ash'ari replies to the Mu'tazili objections that breaking a threat would entail lying, altering speech, and denying eternal punishment for disbelievers.

Core Idea
God's threat is implicitly conditional; forgiveness only for believers.

The Mu'tazilis argued that if God were to break His threat of punishment, it would imply lying, alteration of speech, and ultimately that disbelievers might not be eternally punished. In this passage, Sanusi presents the Ash'ari responses, which defend God's absolute freedom while maintaining the distinction between believers and disbelievers. These responses rely on a nuanced understanding of divine speech and will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the three distinct sections: 'أما عن لزوم الكذب', 'أما عن لزوم تبديل القول', and 'أما استتباعه القول بعدم خلود'.
These three sections correspond to the three Mu'tazili objections.
2
Understand the first response: lying
The Ash'aris argue that a generous person's threat is implicitly conditional on will. So not fulfilling it is not lying. Contrast this with promises, which are unconditional.
They support this with a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ.
3
Understand the second response: alteration of speech
The forbidden alteration is only concerning disbelievers or those whom Allah has not willed forgiveness. This is similar to the first response.
4
Understand the third response: eternal punishment
The Ash'aris do not concede that their position leads to denying eternal punishment for disbelievers. They affirm that disbelief cannot be forgiven, citing Quran 4:48.
Thus forgiveness is restricted to sinful believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أجاب الأشاعرة على ذلك ؛ أما عن لزوم الكذب فقالوا : لا نُسلّم أنه يلزم الكذب ؛ لأنَّ الكريم إذا أخبر بالوعيد فإن اللائق بكرمه أنْ يَبْني إخباره به على المشيئة وإن لم يُصرح بها ؛ فإذا قال: «لأعذبن زيدا» مثلا ، فإنَّ نيَّته أن يعذَّبه إن شاء ؛ فلو لم يعذِّبه لم يكن كاذبا ؛ لأنَّه لم يشأ عذابه ؛ بخلاف الوعد فإنَّ اللائق بالكرم أنْ يَبْني إخبارَهُ على الجزم، وقد وجَدْنَا في الحديث مصداق ذلك، وهو قول النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «من وعده الله على عمل ثوابا فهو مُنجز له، ومَن أوعده على عمل عقابا فهو بالخيار إن شاء عذبه ، وإن شاء غفر له» [مسند أبي يعلى، برقم: ٣٣١٦ . ومسند البزار: ٦٨٨٢] .
وأما عن لزوم تبديل القول: فإن الممنوع إنما هو تبديل القول في وعيد الكفار، أو من لم الله تعالى العفو عنه ، وهو نحو الجواب عن الموضوع السابق . وأما استتباعه القول بعدم خلود الكُفَّار في النَّار : فإِنَّا لا نُسلّم ذلك؛ لأننا نقرر أنه لا يجوز العفو عن الكفر ؛ فيكون ما ذكرناه مقصوراً على عُصاة المؤمنين ، وهذا التخصيص مُستفاد من قوله تعالى: (إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ، وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ) [النساء: ٤٨] .
And the Ash'aris answered that: As for the necessity of lying, they said: We do not concede that lying necessarily follows; because the noble one when he informs of a threat, it is befitting to his generosity that he bases his information on will even if he does not explicitly state it. So if he says: 'I will certainly punish Zayd' for example, his intention is to punish him if He wills; so if he does not punish him, he is not a liar because he did not will his punishment. Unlike the promise, for it is befitting to generosity to base his information on certainty. And we have found confirmation of this in the hadith, which is the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Whoever Allah promises a reward for an action, He will fulfill it for him; and whoever He threatens with punishment for an action, He has the choice: if He wills, He punishes him, and if He wills, He forgives him.' [Musnad Abi Ya'la, no. 3316; Musnad al-Bazzar, no. 6882].
As for the necessity of alteration of speech: what is forbidden is only alteration of speech concerning the threat against disbelievers, or those for whom Allah the Exalted has not willed forgiveness, and it is similar to the answer on the previous topic. As for the entailment of the saying that disbelievers are not eternally in the Fire: we do not concede that; because we affirm that it is not permissible to forgive disbelief; so what we mentioned is restricted to sinful believers. And this specification is derived from His saying the Exalted: {Indeed Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills} [An-Nisa: 48].
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage contains the Ash'ari responses to the three Mu'tazili objections. The response is structured in three points corresponding to the three Mu'tazili arguments. (1) On the accusation of lying: the Ash'aris do not concede that breaking the threat implies lying. They argue that when a generous person makes a threat, it is fitting for his generosity that his statement is implicitly conditional on will, even if not stated. If he says 'I will punish Zayd', his intention is 'if I will'. So if he does not punish, he is not lying because he did not will it. This contrasts with promise, where the fitting thing is to be decisive. They support this with a hadith: the Prophet said that for a promise, Allah fulfills; for a threat, He has the choice to punish or forgive. (2) On alteration of speech: they argue that forbidden alteration is only regarding the threat against disbelievers or those for whom Allah has not willed forgiveness; this is similar to the first point. (3) On denying eternal punishment: they do not concede that it follows, because they affirm that disbelief cannot be forgiven. So the possibility of forgiveness is restricted to sinful believers. This specification is from the verse in An-Nisa that Allah does not forgive shirk but forgives lesser sins for whom He wills. Thus the Ash'ari position does not affect the eternal punishment of disbelievers.

Key Terms
الجواب
الكذب
المشيئة
تبديل القول
الخلود
العفو عن الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris deny eternal punishment of disbelievers because they argue God may not fulfill threats.
Correction: The Ash'aris restrict forgiveness to sinful believers; disbelief is unpardonable, so eternal punishment for disbelievers remains.

Checkpoint
How do Ash'aris answer the Mu'tazili objection that breaking a threat entails lying?
A) They argue that God never breaks His threat.
B) They say the threat is implicitly conditional on will, so not fulfilling it is not lying.
C) They claim the hadith proves threats are always fulfilled.
D) They say lying is permissible for God.

Key Takeaway
Ash'aris defend God's freedom in threat by making it implicitly conditional on will, and uphold eternal punishment for disbelievers by limiting forgiveness to believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live with a genuine fear of God's punishment, or do you presume upon His mercy as if His threats are not serious? How does the Ash'ari teaching that threat is conditional on will affect your sense of accountability?
?
When you sin, do you feel a false sense of security because you know God can forgive, or does His discretion (He may or may not forgive) drive you to repentance? What would change if you took His warnings as absolute?
?
Are you more motivated by hope of reward (promise) or fear of punishment (threat)? Based on this lesson, which should have a greater claim on your heart? What concrete action will you take today to align your life with the weight of both?

The Logical Necessity of Divine Promise and Permissibility of Breaking Threat
Definition and logical proof of the distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational basis for the Ash'ari view that God must fulfil His promises but may withhold His threats.

Core Idea
Keeping a promise is morally necessary; breaking a threat is not.

In this opening passage, the author lays the logical groundwork for the Ash'ari position on divine promises and threats. He argues that since God is perfect, He cannot engage in a deficiency like breaking a promise, whereas withholding a threat does not imply imperfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and the translation. Note the logical structure: if promise broken, then lying, foolishness, etc., which contradicts divine perfection.
The author quotes two Quranic verses to support his point.
2
Identify the key terms
Understand the meanings of wa'd, wa'id, khulf, and irada.
The footnote explains the relation to the eternal will.
3
Contrast the two cases
Notice that the author treats promise as obligatory and threat as permissible. Ask why.
The answer lies in the nature of the action: breaking a promise is a deficiency, but not fulfilling a threat is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات
الأزل (١)؛ إذ المراد لا يتخلَّفُ عن الإرادة؛ لأنَّه لو تخلّف إعطاء الموعود به لزمَ الكِذبُ والسَّفه والخُلْف والتَّبديل في القول، وهو خلاف قوله تعالى: إِنَّكَ لَا تُخلِفُ الْمِيعَادَ) [آل عمران: ١٩٤) مَا يُبَدَّلُ الْقَوْلُ لَدَى [ف: ٢٩]، فالتَّوابُ فضل من الله تعالى وَعَدَ به المُطِيعَ، فيفى له به؛ لأنَّ الخُلْف في الوعد نقص يجب تنزيهه تعالى عنه، بخلاف الوعيد؛ فإنَّه لا يستحيل إخلافه، فيجوز.
وقد أجاب الأشاعرة على ذلك؛ أما عن لزوم الكذب فقالوا: لا نُسلّم أنه يلزم الكذب؛ لأنَّ الكريم إذا أخبر بالوعيد فإن اللائق بكرمه أنْ يَبْني إخباره به على المشيئة وإن لم يُصرح بها؛ فإذا قال: «لأعذبن زيدا» مثلا، فإنَّ نيَّته أن يعذَّبه إن شاء؛ فلو لم يعذِّبه لم يكن كاذبا؛ لأنَّه لم يشأ عذابه؛ بخلاف الوعد فإنَّ اللائق بالكرم أنْ يَبْني إخبارَهُ على الجزم، وقد وجَدْنَا في الحديث مصداق ذلك، وهو قول النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «من وعده الله على عمل ثوابا فهو مُنجز له، ومَن أوعده على عمل عقابا فهو بالخيار إن شاء عذبه، وإن شاء غفر له» [مسند أبي يعلى، برقم: ٣٣١٦ ومسند البزار: ٦٨٨٢].
يرد
وأما عن لزوم تبديل القول: فإن الممنوع إنما هو تبديل القول في وعيد الكفار، أو من لم يرد الله تعالى العفو عنه، وهو نحو الجواب عن الموضوع السابق. وأما استتباعه القول بعدم خلود الكُفَّار في النَّار: فإِنَّا لا نُسلّم ذلك؛ لأننا نقرر أنه لا يجوز العفو عن الكفر؛ فيكون ما ذكرناه مقصوراً على عُصاة المؤمنين، وهذا التخصيص مُستفاد من قوله تعالى: (إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ، وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ) [النساء: ٤٨].
(١) قوله: (الذي سبقت به إرادته الأولى: وعده الذي وعد به على لسان نبيه أو في كتابه، وإلا فالوعد والوعيد بالنظر للإرادة الأزلية لا يتخلفان، وغرضنا التفرقة بينهما أفاده شيخنا، ولك أن تقول: هذا وصف كاشف إشارة إلى أنه يلزم الوعد الإرادة الأزلية ضرورة أنه لا يتخلف، والوعيد قد تسبق الإرادة بغفرانه فتدبر الأمير.
Section of Ilahiyyat. The eternal (al-azal) (1); because the intended (al-murad) does not lag behind the will (al-irada); for if the giving of the promised thing were to lag, lying, foolishness, breaking of promise, and changing of speech would follow, contrary to His statement: 'Indeed, You do not break the promise' [Aal-e-Imran: 194] and 'The word is not changed before Me' [Qaf: 29]. Thus reward (al-thawab) is a favor from Allah, which He promised to the obedient, so He fulfills it for him, because breaking a promise (al-khulf fi al-wa'd) is a deficiency from which Allah must be exalted. Unlike the threat (al-wa'id), for it is not impossible to break it, so it is permissible. The Ash'aris have answered this: As for the necessitation of lying, they said: We do not concede that lying is necessitated; because the generous one, when he informs of a threat, it is befitting to his generosity that he builds his information on the will, even if he does not explicitly state it. If he says, 'I will punish Zayd,' for example, his intention is to punish him if He wills. So if He does not punish him, he is not a liar because He did not will his punishment. Unlike the promise, for it is befitting to generosity that he builds his information on certainty. We have found confirmation of this in the hadith, which is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever Allah promises a reward for an action, He fulfills it for him, and whoever He threatens with punishment for an action, He has the choice: if He wills, He punishes him, and if He wills, He forgives him' [Musnad Abi Ya'la, no. 3316, and Musnad al-Bazzar, no. 6882]. It is objected: As for the necessitation of changing speech, what is prevented is only changing speech in the threat to the disbelievers, or to those for whom Allah has not intended forgiveness, and it is similar to the answer to the previous subject. As for it entailing the statement that the disbelievers will not remain eternally in the Fire, we do not concede that; because we affirm that forgiveness of disbelief is not permissible; so what we have mentioned is restricted to sinning believers. This specification is derived from His statement: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [An-Nisa': 48]. (1) His saying: ('which His first will preceded'): His promise which He promised upon the tongue of His prophet or in His book; otherwise, promise and threat, with regard to the eternal will, do not lag; and our purpose is to differentiate between them, as our teacher taught us. And you may say: this is a descriptive attribute indicating that the promise necessitates the eternal will necessarily because it does not lag, and the threat may be preceded by the will to forgive it. So reflect, O Amir.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari argument regarding divine promises (wa'd) and threats (wa'id). It begins by defining the promise: the intended thing does not lag behind the will, otherwise lying, foolishness, breach of promise, and alteration of speech would occur, contradicting Qur'anic verses that affirm God's faithfulness. Reward (thawab) is a favor promised to the obedient, and God must fulfill it because breaking a promise would be a deficiency unbecoming of His perfection. In contrast, breaking a threat is not impossible, so it is permissible. The Ash'aris then respond to an objection about lying: the objection claims that if God threatens but does not carry it out, He would be lying. The Ash'aris answer that a generous person, when uttering a threat, implicitly conditions it on His will, even if not stated. For example, saying 'I will punish Zayd' means 'if I will it.' If He does not punish, He is not a liar because He did not will it. For a promise, the implication is certainty. This is supported by a hadith where the Prophet states that God fulfills a promise but has choice regarding a threat. Then a second objection is addressed: that changing the threat would be altering speech, which is prohibited. The Ash'aris respond that prohibition of changing speech applies only to threats against disbelievers or those for whom God does not intend forgiveness. As for the implication that this would mean disbelievers are not eternally punished, the Ash'aris reject that because forgiveness of disbelief is impossible; the discussion is restricted to sinning believers, as derived from the verse that God does not forgive shirk but forgives lesser sins for whom He wills. The footnote clarifies that the term 'al-azal' refers to the promise preceded by the first will, emphasizing that promise and threat differ in relation to the eternal will, with the promise being necessary and the threat possibly overtaken by the will to forgive.

Key Terms
وعد (wa'd)
وعيد (wa'id)
خلف (khulf)
إرادة (irada)
مشيئة (mashī'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God's threat is as binding as His promise.
Correction: The passage shows that breaking a threat is permissible and not a deficiency, unlike breaking a promise which would be a deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would be entailed if God did not fulfill His promise?
A) Lying and foolishness
B) Mercy
C) Change of will
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
God must keep His promise because breaking it would be a deficiency, but He may withhold His threat without imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on God's promise of reward but feared His punishment, not realizing the difference? How does knowing God must keep His promise but may withhold threat change your hope in His mercy?
?
If breaking a threat is permissible for God out of mercy, do you still take His warnings seriously? What would it mean for your repentance to truly trust that His mercy can override His threat, while His promise remains certain?
?
When you promise something to someone, do you feel bound because God's own nature requires truthfulness? How can you align your own character with the perfection of God in keeping promises, while also showing mercy like Him in withholding threats?

The Ash'ari Defense Against the Charge of Lying
Objection-and-answer regarding lying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that God's threat is implicitly conditioned on His will, so that withholding the threat does not constitute lying.

Core Idea
Threats are conditional, promises are absolute.

Having established the distinction, the author anticipates an objection: if God threatens but does not carry it out, is He not a liar? The Ash'aris respond by analyzing the nature of speech: a generous person conditions his threat on the will, so if the will does not decree punishment, no lie occurs. This is supported by a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Note the structure: objection stated, then Ash'ari answer.
2
Understand the concept of implicit conditioning
The author uses the analogy of a generous person saying 'I will punish Zayd' meaning 'if I will it.' Thus, if punishment does not happen, no lie.
3
See the hadith evidence
The Prophet explicitly states that God has a choice regarding punishment.
