Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
The Anecdote: Worldly Conditions Are Not Absolute
Anecdote relativizing worldly states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the anecdote of the Jew and the scholar relativizes worldly states and challenges the Mu'tazili assumption that God must provide worldly benefit to the obedient.

Core Idea
Worldly circumstances are not absolute measures of divine favor.

Before diving into the logical arguments, the author presents a vivid anecdote that sets the stage. A shabbily dressed Jew confronts a prominent scholar, using a well-known hadith to question why the scholar enjoys comfort while he suffers. The scholar’s response reveals that the true measure of benefit is the Hereafter, not this world. This story undercuts the Mu’tazili notion that God must always provide the most beneficial worldly outcome.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the contrast between the scholar's apparent comfort and the Jew's misery.
2
Identify the hadith
The Jew quotes the hadith: 'The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever.' Reflect on its meaning.
3
Analyze the scholar's response
The scholar explains that relative to the Hereafter, his situation is a prison and the Jew's is a paradise. Understand the logic of comparison.
This response relativizes worldly states, making them unsuitable as absolute measures of divine benefit.
4
Connect to the Mu'tazili principle
Ask yourself: How does this anecdote challenge the idea that God must always do what is most beneficial in this world?
The story shows that worldly appearances can be deceiving; true benefit is eschatological.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقض قاعدة الصلاح والأصلح الاعتزالية
مَرَّ يوماً بالسُّوق في موكب عظيم وهَيَّاةٍ جَمِيلةٍ، فهجَمَ عليه يهودي وأثوابه مُلَطَّخةٌ بالدَّرَنِ، وهو في غاية الرَّثَاثة والبشاعة ، فقَبَضَ على لِجَامِ بغلته ، ثم قال له: يا شيخ الإسلام، أنت تزعم أن نبيكم قال: «الدنيا سجن المؤمن، وجنة الكافر»، فأي سجن هذا أنتَ فيه مع النعمة ؟ وأي جنَّة أنا فيها مع ما ترى ؟ فقال له الحافظ الله : أما أنا ، فإنَّ الذي أنا فيه بالنسبة لما أعده الله في الآخرة مِن النّعيم للمؤمنين يُعدُّ سجنا ، وأما أنت ، فإن الذي أنت فيه بالنسبة لما ينتظرك من العذاب الأليم يُعَدُّ جَنَّةٌ .
الوجه الثاني: لو كان فعل الأصلح واجبًا على الله لم يستوجب عليه شكرا، لكونه مؤدياً للواجب عليه ، كمَن يرد وديعة أودعها ، وكمن يؤدي دَيْنًا لَزِمَه ، مع أنه سبحانه قد طلب من عباده أن يشكروه على ما فعل معهم ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لِي وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٥٢ ] ، وقال : يُبَنِي إِسْرَاءِيلَ اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَتِيَ الَّتِي أَنْعَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَأَنَى فَضَّلْتُكُمْ عَلَى الْعَالَمِينَ) [البقرة: ٤٧ ] ، وقال : أَنِ اشْكُرْ لِي وَلِوَالِدَيْكَ ﴾ [لقمان: ١٤]، وما لا يحصى من الآيات .
والوجه الثالث: أن مَقدُورَات الله تعالى غير متناهية إلى حد ، وهذا الأصلح الذي أوجبوه عليه تعالى، إما أن يكون معلومَ المِقدار، أي: محدودًا بحدٍ لا يتجاوزه، وإما ألا يكون كذلك ، فإن كان معلوم المقدار محدوداً بحدٍ ينتهي إليه فإن الزيادة على هذا القدر أمر ممكن واقع تحت مقدوره سبحانه ، فلا يكون ما وصل إلى الحد المقدر هو الأصلح؛ لأنَّ الأكثر صلاحاً ممكن ، وإن لم يكن محدوداً بحد لا يتجاوزه، لزم الجهل بحقيقة الواجب. فإن قيل: نختار الأول ، ولا نسلم أنَّ الزِّيادة أصلح ؛ لأنه ربما يصير ضم المزيد مفسدة، كما ضم النافع إلى النافع قد مضرة ، ألا ترى أنَّ الطبيب يصف قَدْرًا مُعيَّنا من الدواء يكون فيه الشَّفاء ، فإذا أضيف قدرٌ آخرُ مِنْه كان مَضرَّةً ، فالجواب: أَنَّا لا تعقل أَنَّ ضَمَّ الصَّلاح إلى الصَّلاح يكون فساداً ، وقياس ذلك على الدواء والعلاج به قياس فاسد ؛ لأن الزيادة في الدواء ليس من باب ضم النافع إلى النَّافع ، بل هو من باب ضمّ غيرِ النَّافع ؛ بل الضار إلى النافع ، ألا ترى أنه يطلب في الحمى مثلا شراب قدرٍ معلوم من الدواء، يقاوم الحَرَارة الَّتِي تغلب في مثل هذه الحال، فإذا زيدَ على القَدْرِ المطلوب قَدْرٌ آخرُ فَإِنَّ هذا القَدْرَ الزَّائِدَ لا يعمل عمل القدر المطلوب من دفع الحرارة ، وإنما يثبت برودة تزيل الصحة والاعتدال .
الوجه الرابع : أنَّه يلزم على ما ذهبوا إليه أن تكون إماتة الأنبياء والمرشدين بعد حين من حياتهم مع تبقية إبليسَ وذُرِّياته من الضالين المُضلين إلى يوم الدين أصلح عندكم لعباد الله ، وكفى بهذا فظاعة.
الوجه الخامس : أنه يلزم على مذهبهم أن الله تعالى لم يفعل ما وجب عليه مع كلِّ مِمَّن عاش سليما حتى بلغ وكفر أو او ارتد بعد الإسلام، لأنَّ إماتته في حال الصبي أو سَلْبَ عقله كان أصلح له، ولم يفعله ، فإن زعمتم أنَّ الأصلح هو التكليف والتعريض للنعيم المقيم لكون ذلك أعلى المَنْزِلَتَيْنِ، وقد فعله هؤلاء الذين ذكرتم، قلنا: فلا يكون قد فعل ما هو الأصلح بكلِّ مَن أماته في حال الصبى أو أورثه الجنونَ ؛ لأنَّه لم يبق واحدا من هؤلاء حتى يبلغ سليما فيعرضه لأعلى المنزلتين. فإن قيل : عَلِم مِن هؤلاء أنَّ واحدا منهم لو عاش لضلّ وأَضَلَّ غيره فأماته لمصلحته ومصلحة غيره ، قلنا : فلِمَ لم يُمِتْ «فِرعَوْنَ» و«هامان» «ومَزْدَكَ» وزَرَادِشْتَ» وغيرهم مِن الضَّالِّين والمضلين أطفالاً ؛ وهذا الوجه هو لباب المناقشة التي دارت بين أبي هاشم الجُبَّائي وأبي الحسن الأشعري ، وكان الأشعري أحد تلامذة الجبائي ، وكان الشيخ يُقرِّرُ في درسه يوما هذه المسألة ، فقال أبو الحسن: ما تقول في ثلاثة إخوة مات أحدهم كبيرًا طائعاً ، ومات الثاني كبيرًا عاصياً ، ومات الثالث صغيرًا ؟ فقال الجبائي : الأول يُثاب بالجنة ، والثاني يُثاب بالنار ، والثالث لا يثاب ولا يعاقب ؛ (وذلك على قولهم بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين). فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثالث : يا ربِّ ، لأيِّ شَيْءٍ أَمَتَنِي صغيرًا ولم تُبقنِي حتى أبلغ فأطيعك فأدخل الجنَّةَ ؟
فقال الجبائي: يقول له ربُّه: علمتُ أنك لو كبرت عصيت فتدخل النَّار، فكانَ الأصلح لك أن تموت صغيرًا. فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثَّاني: يا ربِّ لَمَّا عَلِمْتَ أَنِّي إنْ كبرتُ عصيتُ فدخلتُ النَّارَ ، فلِمَ لم تمتني صغيرًا حَتَّى أكون كأخي ؟ ماذا يقول الرَّبُّ ؟ فَبُهِتَ الجبائي . تُمِثْنِي ومن ذلك الحين ترك الأشعري دروسه ومذهبه واشتغل هو وأتباعه بإبطال مذهب
Refutation of the Mu'tazili principle of al-salah (what is beneficial) and al-aslah (what is most beneficial). He passed one day through the market in a great procession and beautiful commotion, then a Jew rushed upon him with his garments soiled with filth, and he was in extreme shabbiness and ugliness. He grabbed the bridle of his mule and said to him: O Shaykh al-Islam, you claim that your Prophet said: 'The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever.' So what prison is this that you are in with the blessing? And what paradise am I in with what you see? So al-Hafiz [؟] said to him: As for me, what I am in, compared to what God has prepared in the Hereafter of bliss for the believers, is considered a prison. And as for you, what you are in, compared to what awaits you of painful punishment, is considered a paradise. The second aspect: If doing what is most beneficial (al-aslah) were obligatory upon God, He would not deserve thanks for it, because He would be performing an obligation upon Him, like one who returns a deposit entrusted to him, and like one who pays a debt owed by him, whereas He, exalted, has asked His servants to thank Him for what He has done with them. God Almighty said: 'And be grateful to Me and do not deny Me' [2:152], and He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My favor which I bestowed upon you and that I preferred you over the worlds' [2:47], and He said: 'Be grateful to Me and to your parents' [31:14], and countless verses. The third aspect: The capabilities of God Almighty are infinite without limit. This most beneficial (al-aslah) which they have made obligatory upon Him, exalted, is either of known measure, i.e., limited by a limit it does not exceed, or it is not so. If it is of known measure, limited by a limit at which it ends, then an increase beyond this measure is a possible matter falling under His power, exalted, so what has reached the limit determined is not the most beneficial, because what is more beneficial is possible. And if it is not limited by a limit it does not exceed, ignorance of the reality of the obligatory necessarily follows. If it is said: We choose the first, and we do not concede that the increase is more beneficial, because perhaps adding more may cause corruption, just as adding beneficial to beneficial may be harmful. Do you not see that the physician prescribes a specific amount of medicine in which there is healing, and if he adds another amount from it, it causes harm? So the answer: We do not conceive that adding benefit to benefit is corruption, and analogizing that to medicine and treatment with it is a corrupt analogy, because the increase in medicine is not of the type of adding beneficial to beneficial, but rather it is of the type of adding what is not beneficial, indeed harmful, to beneficial. Do you not see that in fever, for example, a certain amount of medicine is sought to resist the heat that prevails in such a condition, and if an additional amount is added to the required amount, then this additional amount does not work the work of the required amount of repelling heat, but rather establishes a coldness that removes health and balance. The fourth aspect: It necessarily follows from what they have held that causing the death of the prophets and guides after a time of their lives, while leaving Iblis and his descendants among the misguided misleaders until the Day of Judgment, is most beneficial (aslah) in your view for the servants of God. Enough of this as an atrocity. The fifth aspect: It necessarily follows from their doctrine that God Almighty did not do what was obligatory upon Him with everyone who lived soundly until he reached maturity and disbelieved or apostatized after Islam, because causing him to die as a child or depriving him of his intellect would have been most beneficial for him, but He did not do it. If you claim that the most beneficial is the obligation and exposure to eternal bliss because that is the higher of the two stations, and He has done this to those you mentioned, we say: Then He has not done what is most beneficial to everyone whom He caused to die as a child or inflicted with insanity, because He did not keep any of these until they reached maturity soundly so as to expose them to the higher of the two stations. If it is said: He knew among these that if any of them lived, he would go astray and lead others astray, so He caused him to die for his benefit and the benefit of others. We say: So why did He not cause Pharaoh, Haman, Mazdak, Zardasht, and others among the misguided misleaders to die as children? And this aspect is the core of the debate that took place between Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Al-Ash'ari was one of al-Jubba'i's students, and the teacher (al-Jubba'i) was one day expounding this issue in his lesson. So Abu al-Hasan said: What do you say about three brothers: one died as an adult obedient, the second died as an adult disobedient, and the third died as a child? Al-Jubba'i said: The first is rewarded with Paradise, the second is punished with Hellfire, and the third is neither rewarded nor punished (that according to their doctrine of the station between the two stations). Al-Ash'ari said: If the third says: O Lord, why did You cause me to die as a child and not keep me until I grew up so that I would obey You and enter Paradise? Al-Jubba'i said: His Lord says to him: I knew that if you grew up you would disobey and enter Hellfire, so the most beneficial for you was that you die as a child. Al-Ash'ari said: If the second says: O Lord, since You knew that if I grew up I would disobey and enter Hellfire, why did You not cause me to die as a child so that I would be like my brother? What does the Lord say? Al-Jubba'i was dumbfounded. [؟] And from that time, al-Ash'ari left his (al-Jubba'i's) lessons and doctrine, and he and his followers occupied themselves with refuting the doctrine
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive refutation of the Mu'tazili principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-aslah) for His creatures. The author presents five distinct arguments (wujuh) against this doctrine, preceded by an anecdote that illustrates the relativity of worldly states. The anecdote: A Jew confronts a Hanbali scholar (likely Ibn al-Jawzi) with the hadith that the world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever, pointing out the scholar's comfort versus his own misery. The scholar replies that relative to the Hereafter, the believer's state is like a prison and the disbeliever's like a paradise. This sets up the idea that limited worldly evaluations do not determine divine obligation. The first argument: If doing the most beneficial were obligatory on God, then He would not deserve thanks for it, since one is not thanked for fulfilling an obligation. But God commands gratitude, implying His acts are favors, not duties. The second argument: God's power is infinite; if the most beneficial were limited, an increase would be possible, contradicting its being the most. If unlimited, the obligation is unknowable. An objection likens this to medicine where excess harms. The author rebuts that divine benefits do not behave like material substances; adding benefit to benefit never becomes corruption. The third argument: The Mu'tazili view leads to the absurdity that killing prophets while leaving Iblis alive is more beneficial, which is plainly repugnant. The fourth argument: It also implies that God fails to do the most beneficial for those who reach maturity and disbelieve, since death in childhood would have been better. A counter-argument about foreknowledge of future evil is answered by pointing out that the same logic would require all tyrants to die as children. The passage culminates in the famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his teacher al-Jubba'i: three brothers—one obedient adult, one disobedient adult, one child. Al-Jubba'i's position leads to an inconsistency when the disobedient brother asks why God did not let him die as a child. Al-Jubba'i is silenced, and this impasse reportedly caused al-Ash'ari to abandon Mu'tazilism. The commentary follows the sequence: anecdote, then the five aspects in order, preserving the logical flow and the final story.

Key Terms
الصلاح
الأصلح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That worldly prosperity or adversity directly reflects God's favor or disfavor.
Correction: Worldly conditions are not absolute indicators; true benefit is eschatological, as shown by the scholar's response.

Checkpoint
In the anecdote, how does the scholar justify his statement that he is in a prison?
A) He claims his wealth is actually a burden.
B) He compares his current state to the eternal bliss of Paradise.
C) He says the Jew's poverty is a punishment.
D) He admits the hadith is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The anecdote teaches that worldly conditions are relative and cannot be used to argue that God must do what is most beneficial in this life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience hardship in this world, do you ever doubt that Allah loves you? How does this anecdote reframe your suffering? What will you say to yourself the next time that doubt creeps in?
?
Think of a non-Muslim who enjoys worldly luxury while you struggle. Does that ever cause you to question Allah's wisdom? After reading this lesson, how should you view that person's 'paradise'? Write a specific commitment to refocus your heart on the eternal scale.
?
If you were to die today, would you consider your worldly life a 'prison' that led to Paradise, or a temporary comfort that you are reluctant to leave? Be honest: what does your answer reveal about your attachment to this world? What one change will you make today to loosen that grip?

Divine Attributes
intermediate

First Argument: Obligation Negates Gratitude
First argument: obligation versus gratitude

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming that doing the most beneficial is obligatory upon God would eliminate the basis for divine gratitude commanded in the Quran.

Core Idea
If God were obliged to benefit us, He would not deserve thanks.

The author’s first formal argument is a logical and scriptural one. The Mu’tazilites hold that God must do what is most beneficial for His creatures. But if that act were a duty, God would simply be fulfilling an obligation, much like returning a deposit. No one thanks a person for doing what he must. Yet the Quran repeatedly commands gratitude to God for His favors. This contradiction shows that the Mu’tazili premise is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the key point: obligation negates gratitude.
2
Identify the analogy
The author compares an obligatory act to returning a deposit or paying a debt. Understand why such acts do not warrant thanks.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites three verses commanding gratitude. Reflect on how these verses presuppose that God’s favors are voluntary, not obligatory.
4
Formulate the contradiction
If obligation eliminates the need for thanks, but God commands thanks, then the Mu'tazili claim is inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقض قاعدة الصلاح والأصلح الاعتزالية
مَرَّ يوماً بالسُّوق في موكب عظيم وهَيَّاةٍ جَمِيلةٍ، فهجَمَ عليه يهودي وأثوابه مُلَطَّخةٌ بالدَّرَنِ، وهو في غاية الرَّثَاثة والبشاعة ، فقَبَضَ على لِجَامِ بغلته ، ثم قال له: يا شيخ الإسلام، أنت تزعم أن نبيكم قال: «الدنيا سجن المؤمن، وجنة الكافر»، فأي سجن هذا أنتَ فيه مع النعمة ؟ وأي جنَّة أنا فيها مع ما ترى ؟ فقال له الحافظ الله : أما أنا ، فإنَّ الذي أنا فيه بالنسبة لما أعده الله في الآخرة مِن النّعيم للمؤمنين يُعدُّ سجنا ، وأما أنت ، فإن الذي أنت فيه بالنسبة لما ينتظرك من العذاب الأليم يُعَدُّ جَنَّةٌ .
الوجه الثاني: لو كان فعل الأصلح واجبًا على الله لم يستوجب عليه شكرا، لكونه مؤدياً للواجب عليه ، كمَن يرد وديعة أودعها ، وكمن يؤدي دَيْنًا لَزِمَه ، مع أنه سبحانه قد طلب من عباده أن يشكروه على ما فعل معهم ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لِي وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٥٢ ] ، وقال : يُبَنِي إِسْرَاءِيلَ اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَتِيَ الَّتِي أَنْعَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَأَنَى فَضَّلْتُكُمْ عَلَى الْعَالَمِينَ) [البقرة: ٤٧ ] ، وقال : أَنِ اشْكُرْ لِي وَلِوَالِدَيْكَ ﴾ [لقمان: ١٤]، وما لا يحصى من الآيات .
والوجه الثالث: أن مَقدُورَات الله تعالى غير متناهية إلى حد ، وهذا الأصلح الذي أوجبوه عليه تعالى، إما أن يكون معلومَ المِقدار، أي: محدودًا بحدٍ لا يتجاوزه، وإما ألا يكون كذلك ، فإن كان معلوم المقدار محدوداً بحدٍ ينتهي إليه فإن الزيادة على هذا القدر أمر ممكن واقع تحت مقدوره سبحانه ، فلا يكون ما وصل إلى الحد المقدر هو الأصلح؛ لأنَّ الأكثر صلاحاً ممكن ، وإن لم يكن محدوداً بحد لا يتجاوزه، لزم الجهل بحقيقة الواجب. فإن قيل: نختار الأول ، ولا نسلم أنَّ الزِّيادة أصلح ؛ لأنه ربما يصير ضم المزيد مفسدة، كما ضم النافع إلى النافع قد مضرة ، ألا ترى أنَّ الطبيب يصف قَدْرًا مُعيَّنا من الدواء يكون فيه الشَّفاء ، فإذا أضيف قدرٌ آخرُ مِنْه كان مَضرَّةً ، فالجواب: أَنَّا لا تعقل أَنَّ ضَمَّ الصَّلاح إلى الصَّلاح يكون فساداً ، وقياس ذلك على الدواء والعلاج به قياس فاسد ؛ لأن الزيادة في الدواء ليس من باب ضم النافع إلى النَّافع ، بل هو من باب ضمّ غيرِ النَّافع ؛ بل الضار إلى النافع ، ألا ترى أنه يطلب في الحمى مثلا شراب قدرٍ معلوم من الدواء، يقاوم الحَرَارة الَّتِي تغلب في مثل هذه الحال، فإذا زيدَ على القَدْرِ المطلوب قَدْرٌ آخرُ فَإِنَّ هذا القَدْرَ الزَّائِدَ لا يعمل عمل القدر المطلوب من دفع الحرارة ، وإنما يثبت برودة تزيل الصحة والاعتدال .
الوجه الرابع : أنَّه يلزم على ما ذهبوا إليه أن تكون إماتة الأنبياء والمرشدين بعد حين من حياتهم مع تبقية إبليسَ وذُرِّياته من الضالين المُضلين إلى يوم الدين أصلح عندكم لعباد الله ، وكفى بهذا فظاعة.
الوجه الخامس : أنه يلزم على مذهبهم أن الله تعالى لم يفعل ما وجب عليه مع كلِّ مِمَّن عاش سليما حتى بلغ وكفر أو او ارتد بعد الإسلام، لأنَّ إماتته في حال الصبي أو سَلْبَ عقله كان أصلح له، ولم يفعله ، فإن زعمتم أنَّ الأصلح هو التكليف والتعريض للنعيم المقيم لكون ذلك أعلى المَنْزِلَتَيْنِ، وقد فعله هؤلاء الذين ذكرتم، قلنا: فلا يكون قد فعل ما هو الأصلح بكلِّ مَن أماته في حال الصبى أو أورثه الجنونَ ؛ لأنَّه لم يبق واحدا من هؤلاء حتى يبلغ سليما فيعرضه لأعلى المنزلتين. فإن قيل : عَلِم مِن هؤلاء أنَّ واحدا منهم لو عاش لضلّ وأَضَلَّ غيره فأماته لمصلحته ومصلحة غيره ، قلنا : فلِمَ لم يُمِتْ «فِرعَوْنَ» و«هامان» «ومَزْدَكَ» وزَرَادِشْتَ» وغيرهم مِن الضَّالِّين والمضلين أطفالاً ؛ وهذا الوجه هو لباب المناقشة التي دارت بين أبي هاشم الجُبَّائي وأبي الحسن الأشعري ، وكان الأشعري أحد تلامذة الجبائي ، وكان الشيخ يُقرِّرُ في درسه يوما هذه المسألة ، فقال أبو الحسن: ما تقول في ثلاثة إخوة مات أحدهم كبيرًا طائعاً ، ومات الثاني كبيرًا عاصياً ، ومات الثالث صغيرًا ؟ فقال الجبائي : الأول يُثاب بالجنة ، والثاني يُثاب بالنار ، والثالث لا يثاب ولا يعاقب ؛ (وذلك على قولهم بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين). فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثالث : يا ربِّ ، لأيِّ شَيْءٍ أَمَتَنِي صغيرًا ولم تُبقنِي حتى أبلغ فأطيعك فأدخل الجنَّةَ ؟
فقال الجبائي: يقول له ربُّه: علمتُ أنك لو كبرت عصيت فتدخل النَّار، فكانَ الأصلح لك أن تموت صغيرًا. فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثَّاني: يا ربِّ لَمَّا عَلِمْتَ أَنِّي إنْ كبرتُ عصيتُ فدخلتُ النَّارَ ، فلِمَ لم تمتني صغيرًا حَتَّى أكون كأخي ؟ ماذا يقول الرَّبُّ ؟ فَبُهِتَ الجبائي . تُمِثْنِي ومن ذلك الحين ترك الأشعري دروسه ومذهبه واشتغل هو وأتباعه بإبطال مذهب
Refutation of the Mu'tazili principle of al-salah (what is beneficial) and al-aslah (what is most beneficial). He passed one day through the market in a great procession and beautiful commotion, then a Jew rushed upon him with his garments soiled with filth, and he was in extreme shabbiness and ugliness. He grabbed the bridle of his mule and said to him: O Shaykh al-Islam, you claim that your Prophet said: 'The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever.' So what prison is this that you are in with the blessing? And what paradise am I in with what you see? So al-Hafiz [؟] said to him: As for me, what I am in, compared to what God has prepared in the Hereafter of bliss for the believers, is considered a prison. And as for you, what you are in, compared to what awaits you of painful punishment, is considered a paradise. The second aspect: If doing what is most beneficial (al-aslah) were obligatory upon God, He would not deserve thanks for it, because He would be performing an obligation upon Him, like one who returns a deposit entrusted to him, and like one who pays a debt owed by him, whereas He, exalted, has asked His servants to thank Him for what He has done with them. God Almighty said: 'And be grateful to Me and do not deny Me' [2:152], and He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My favor which I bestowed upon you and that I preferred you over the worlds' [2:47], and He said: 'Be grateful to Me and to your parents' [31:14], and countless verses. The third aspect: The capabilities of God Almighty are infinite without limit. This most beneficial (al-aslah) which they have made obligatory upon Him, exalted, is either of known measure, i.e., limited by a limit it does not exceed, or it is not so. If it is of known measure, limited by a limit at which it ends, then an increase beyond this measure is a possible matter falling under His power, exalted, so what has reached the limit determined is not the most beneficial, because what is more beneficial is possible. And if it is not limited by a limit it does not exceed, ignorance of the reality of the obligatory necessarily follows. If it is said: We choose the first, and we do not concede that the increase is more beneficial, because perhaps adding more may cause corruption, just as adding beneficial to beneficial may be harmful. Do you not see that the physician prescribes a specific amount of medicine in which there is healing, and if he adds another amount from it, it causes harm? So the answer: We do not conceive that adding benefit to benefit is corruption, and analogizing that to medicine and treatment with it is a corrupt analogy, because the increase in medicine is not of the type of adding beneficial to beneficial, but rather it is of the type of adding what is not beneficial, indeed harmful, to beneficial. Do you not see that in fever, for example, a certain amount of medicine is sought to resist the heat that prevails in such a condition, and if an additional amount is added to the required amount, then this additional amount does not work the work of the required amount of repelling heat, but rather establishes a coldness that removes health and balance. The fourth aspect: It necessarily follows from what they have held that causing the death of the prophets and guides after a time of their lives, while leaving Iblis and his descendants among the misguided misleaders until the Day of Judgment, is most beneficial (aslah) in your view for the servants of God. Enough of this as an atrocity. The fifth aspect: It necessarily follows from their doctrine that God Almighty did not do what was obligatory upon Him with everyone who lived soundly until he reached maturity and disbelieved or apostatized after Islam, because causing him to die as a child or depriving him of his intellect would have been most beneficial for him, but He did not do it. If you claim that the most beneficial is the obligation and exposure to eternal bliss because that is the higher of the two stations, and He has done this to those you mentioned, we say: Then He has not done what is most beneficial to everyone whom He caused to die as a child or inflicted with insanity, because He did not keep any of these until they reached maturity soundly so as to expose them to the higher of the two stations. If it is said: He knew among these that if any of them lived, he would go astray and lead others astray, so He caused him to die for his benefit and the benefit of others. We say: So why did He not cause Pharaoh, Haman, Mazdak, Zardasht, and others among the misguided misleaders to die as children? And this aspect is the core of the debate that took place between Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Al-Ash'ari was one of al-Jubba'i's students, and the teacher (al-Jubba'i) was one day expounding this issue in his lesson. So Abu al-Hasan said: What do you say about three brothers: one died as an adult obedient, the second died as an adult disobedient, and the third died as a child? Al-Jubba'i said: The first is rewarded with Paradise, the second is punished with Hellfire, and the third is neither rewarded nor punished (that according to their doctrine of the station between the two stations). Al-Ash'ari said: If the third says: O Lord, why did You cause me to die as a child and not keep me until I grew up so that I would obey You and enter Paradise? Al-Jubba'i said: His Lord says to him: I knew that if you grew up you would disobey and enter Hellfire, so the most beneficial for you was that you die as a child. Al-Ash'ari said: If the second says: O Lord, since You knew that if I grew up I would disobey and enter Hellfire, why did You not cause me to die as a child so that I would be like my brother? What does the Lord say? Al-Jubba'i was dumbfounded. [؟] And from that time, al-Ash'ari left his (al-Jubba'i's) lessons and doctrine, and he and his followers occupied themselves with refuting the doctrine
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive refutation of the Mu'tazili principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-aslah) for His creatures. The author presents five distinct arguments (wujuh) against this doctrine, preceded by an anecdote that illustrates the relativity of worldly states. The anecdote: A Jew confronts a Hanbali scholar (likely Ibn al-Jawzi) with the hadith that the world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever, pointing out the scholar's comfort versus his own misery. The scholar replies that relative to the Hereafter, the believer's state is like a prison and the disbeliever's like a paradise. This sets up the idea that limited worldly evaluations do not determine divine obligation. The first argument: If doing the most beneficial were obligatory on God, then He would not deserve thanks for it, since one is not thanked for fulfilling an obligation. But God commands gratitude, implying His acts are favors, not duties. The second argument: God's power is infinite; if the most beneficial were limited, an increase would be possible, contradicting its being the most. If unlimited, the obligation is unknowable. An objection likens this to medicine where excess harms. The author rebuts that divine benefits do not behave like material substances; adding benefit to benefit never becomes corruption. The third argument: The Mu'tazili view leads to the absurdity that killing prophets while leaving Iblis alive is more beneficial, which is plainly repugnant. The fourth argument: It also implies that God fails to do the most beneficial for those who reach maturity and disbelieve, since death in childhood would have been better. A counter-argument about foreknowledge of future evil is answered by pointing out that the same logic would require all tyrants to die as children. The passage culminates in the famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his teacher al-Jubba'i: three brothers—one obedient adult, one disobedient adult, one child. Al-Jubba'i's position leads to an inconsistency when the disobedient brother asks why God did not let him die as a child. Al-Jubba'i is silenced, and this impasse reportedly caused al-Ash'ari to abandon Mu'tazilism. The commentary follows the sequence: anecdote, then the five aspects in order, preserving the logical flow and the final story.

Key Terms
الوجوب
الشكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's obligation to do good is compatible with being thanked for it.
Correction: One does not thank a person for fulfilling a duty; Quranic gratitude shows God's acts are favors, not obligations.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, why would God not deserve thanks if al-aslah were obligatory?
A) Because God is self-sufficient and does not need thanks.
B) Because an obligatory act is like a debt paid or deposit returned, which does not merit gratitude.
C) Because the Quran commands gratitude only for voluntary acts.
D) Because the Mu'tazilites themselves do not require gratitude.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic command to thank God proves that His favors are voluntary, not obligatory, refuting the Mu'tazili claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a blessing you received today. Did you consider it a gift or something you deserved? How does this lesson expose the difference between obligations and voluntary generosity, and how does that change your attitude toward that blessing?
?
If God were obliged to give you everything good, would you ever feel genuine gratitude? Examine your own heart: have you ever felt entitled to God's favors? What would it take to truly thank Him as a free gift?
?
The analogy of returning a deposit: when you do what is required, you don't expect thanks. When was the last time you thanked God deeply for something you know you didn't deserve? Commit to making that gratitude specific and personal today.

Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
Second Argument: The Infinity Dilemma
Dilemma of infinite power vs defined best

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dilemma that God's infinite power poses for the concept of a single 'most beneficial' act.

Core Idea
If God's power is infinite, no single act can be the 'most beneficial'.

The second argument targets the very definability of 'most beneficial'. The author points out that God’s power is infinite, so any proposed ‘most beneficial’ act would either have a limit (allowing a better one) or be unlimited (making the obligation unknowable). The Mu’tazilite might object by analogy to medicine, where excess is harmful. But the author refutes that analogy, arguing that divine benefits do not behave like material substances.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Read the Arabic passage. Notice the two horns: al-aslah either has a known measure or not.
2
Analyze the first horn
If it has a known measure, an increase is possible, so it would not be the 'most' beneficial. Understand why.
3
Analyze the second horn
If it does not have a known measure, then the obligation is unknowable. Grasp the problem.
4
Examine the objection and rebuttal
The Mu'tazilite objects using the medicine analogy. The author rebuts by showing the analogy fails because divine benefits do not turn harmful when added.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقض قاعدة الصلاح والأصلح الاعتزالية
مَرَّ يوماً بالسُّوق في موكب عظيم وهَيَّاةٍ جَمِيلةٍ، فهجَمَ عليه يهودي وأثوابه مُلَطَّخةٌ بالدَّرَنِ، وهو في غاية الرَّثَاثة والبشاعة ، فقَبَضَ على لِجَامِ بغلته ، ثم قال له: يا شيخ الإسلام، أنت تزعم أن نبيكم قال: «الدنيا سجن المؤمن، وجنة الكافر»، فأي سجن هذا أنتَ فيه مع النعمة ؟ وأي جنَّة أنا فيها مع ما ترى ؟ فقال له الحافظ الله : أما أنا ، فإنَّ الذي أنا فيه بالنسبة لما أعده الله في الآخرة مِن النّعيم للمؤمنين يُعدُّ سجنا ، وأما أنت ، فإن الذي أنت فيه بالنسبة لما ينتظرك من العذاب الأليم يُعَدُّ جَنَّةٌ .
الوجه الثاني: لو كان فعل الأصلح واجبًا على الله لم يستوجب عليه شكرا، لكونه مؤدياً للواجب عليه ، كمَن يرد وديعة أودعها ، وكمن يؤدي دَيْنًا لَزِمَه ، مع أنه سبحانه قد طلب من عباده أن يشكروه على ما فعل معهم ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لِي وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٥٢ ] ، وقال : يُبَنِي إِسْرَاءِيلَ اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَتِيَ الَّتِي أَنْعَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَأَنَى فَضَّلْتُكُمْ عَلَى الْعَالَمِينَ) [البقرة: ٤٧ ] ، وقال : أَنِ اشْكُرْ لِي وَلِوَالِدَيْكَ ﴾ [لقمان: ١٤]، وما لا يحصى من الآيات .
والوجه الثالث: أن مَقدُورَات الله تعالى غير متناهية إلى حد ، وهذا الأصلح الذي أوجبوه عليه تعالى، إما أن يكون معلومَ المِقدار، أي: محدودًا بحدٍ لا يتجاوزه، وإما ألا يكون كذلك ، فإن كان معلوم المقدار محدوداً بحدٍ ينتهي إليه فإن الزيادة على هذا القدر أمر ممكن واقع تحت مقدوره سبحانه ، فلا يكون ما وصل إلى الحد المقدر هو الأصلح؛ لأنَّ الأكثر صلاحاً ممكن ، وإن لم يكن محدوداً بحد لا يتجاوزه، لزم الجهل بحقيقة الواجب. فإن قيل: نختار الأول ، ولا نسلم أنَّ الزِّيادة أصلح ؛ لأنه ربما يصير ضم المزيد مفسدة، كما ضم النافع إلى النافع قد مضرة ، ألا ترى أنَّ الطبيب يصف قَدْرًا مُعيَّنا من الدواء يكون فيه الشَّفاء ، فإذا أضيف قدرٌ آخرُ مِنْه كان مَضرَّةً ، فالجواب: أَنَّا لا تعقل أَنَّ ضَمَّ الصَّلاح إلى الصَّلاح يكون فساداً ، وقياس ذلك على الدواء والعلاج به قياس فاسد ؛ لأن الزيادة في الدواء ليس من باب ضم النافع إلى النَّافع ، بل هو من باب ضمّ غيرِ النَّافع ؛ بل الضار إلى النافع ، ألا ترى أنه يطلب في الحمى مثلا شراب قدرٍ معلوم من الدواء، يقاوم الحَرَارة الَّتِي تغلب في مثل هذه الحال، فإذا زيدَ على القَدْرِ المطلوب قَدْرٌ آخرُ فَإِنَّ هذا القَدْرَ الزَّائِدَ لا يعمل عمل القدر المطلوب من دفع الحرارة ، وإنما يثبت برودة تزيل الصحة والاعتدال .
الوجه الرابع : أنَّه يلزم على ما ذهبوا إليه أن تكون إماتة الأنبياء والمرشدين بعد حين من حياتهم مع تبقية إبليسَ وذُرِّياته من الضالين المُضلين إلى يوم الدين أصلح عندكم لعباد الله ، وكفى بهذا فظاعة.
الوجه الخامس : أنه يلزم على مذهبهم أن الله تعالى لم يفعل ما وجب عليه مع كلِّ مِمَّن عاش سليما حتى بلغ وكفر أو او ارتد بعد الإسلام، لأنَّ إماتته في حال الصبي أو سَلْبَ عقله كان أصلح له، ولم يفعله ، فإن زعمتم أنَّ الأصلح هو التكليف والتعريض للنعيم المقيم لكون ذلك أعلى المَنْزِلَتَيْنِ، وقد فعله هؤلاء الذين ذكرتم، قلنا: فلا يكون قد فعل ما هو الأصلح بكلِّ مَن أماته في حال الصبى أو أورثه الجنونَ ؛ لأنَّه لم يبق واحدا من هؤلاء حتى يبلغ سليما فيعرضه لأعلى المنزلتين. فإن قيل : عَلِم مِن هؤلاء أنَّ واحدا منهم لو عاش لضلّ وأَضَلَّ غيره فأماته لمصلحته ومصلحة غيره ، قلنا : فلِمَ لم يُمِتْ «فِرعَوْنَ» و«هامان» «ومَزْدَكَ» وزَرَادِشْتَ» وغيرهم مِن الضَّالِّين والمضلين أطفالاً ؛ وهذا الوجه هو لباب المناقشة التي دارت بين أبي هاشم الجُبَّائي وأبي الحسن الأشعري ، وكان الأشعري أحد تلامذة الجبائي ، وكان الشيخ يُقرِّرُ في درسه يوما هذه المسألة ، فقال أبو الحسن: ما تقول في ثلاثة إخوة مات أحدهم كبيرًا طائعاً ، ومات الثاني كبيرًا عاصياً ، ومات الثالث صغيرًا ؟ فقال الجبائي : الأول يُثاب بالجنة ، والثاني يُثاب بالنار ، والثالث لا يثاب ولا يعاقب ؛ (وذلك على قولهم بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين). فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثالث : يا ربِّ ، لأيِّ شَيْءٍ أَمَتَنِي صغيرًا ولم تُبقنِي حتى أبلغ فأطيعك فأدخل الجنَّةَ ؟
فقال الجبائي: يقول له ربُّه: علمتُ أنك لو كبرت عصيت فتدخل النَّار، فكانَ الأصلح لك أن تموت صغيرًا. فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثَّاني: يا ربِّ لَمَّا عَلِمْتَ أَنِّي إنْ كبرتُ عصيتُ فدخلتُ النَّارَ ، فلِمَ لم تمتني صغيرًا حَتَّى أكون كأخي ؟ ماذا يقول الرَّبُّ ؟ فَبُهِتَ الجبائي . تُمِثْنِي ومن ذلك الحين ترك الأشعري دروسه ومذهبه واشتغل هو وأتباعه بإبطال مذهب
Refutation of the Mu'tazili principle of al-salah (what is beneficial) and al-aslah (what is most beneficial). He passed one day through the market in a great procession and beautiful commotion, then a Jew rushed upon him with his garments soiled with filth, and he was in extreme shabbiness and ugliness. He grabbed the bridle of his mule and said to him: O Shaykh al-Islam, you claim that your Prophet said: 'The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever.' So what prison is this that you are in with the blessing? And what paradise am I in with what you see? So al-Hafiz [؟] said to him: As for me, what I am in, compared to what God has prepared in the Hereafter of bliss for the believers, is considered a prison. And as for you, what you are in, compared to what awaits you of painful punishment, is considered a paradise. The second aspect: If doing what is most beneficial (al-aslah) were obligatory upon God, He would not deserve thanks for it, because He would be performing an obligation upon Him, like one who returns a deposit entrusted to him, and like one who pays a debt owed by him, whereas He, exalted, has asked His servants to thank Him for what He has done with them. God Almighty said: 'And be grateful to Me and do not deny Me' [2:152], and He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My favor which I bestowed upon you and that I preferred you over the worlds' [2:47], and He said: 'Be grateful to Me and to your parents' [31:14], and countless verses. The third aspect: The capabilities of God Almighty are infinite without limit. This most beneficial (al-aslah) which they have made obligatory upon Him, exalted, is either of known measure, i.e., limited by a limit it does not exceed, or it is not so. If it is of known measure, limited by a limit at which it ends, then an increase beyond this measure is a possible matter falling under His power, exalted, so what has reached the limit determined is not the most beneficial, because what is more beneficial is possible. And if it is not limited by a limit it does not exceed, ignorance of the reality of the obligatory necessarily follows. If it is said: We choose the first, and we do not concede that the increase is more beneficial, because perhaps adding more may cause corruption, just as adding beneficial to beneficial may be harmful. Do you not see that the physician prescribes a specific amount of medicine in which there is healing, and if he adds another amount from it, it causes harm? So the answer: We do not conceive that adding benefit to benefit is corruption, and analogizing that to medicine and treatment with it is a corrupt analogy, because the increase in medicine is not of the type of adding beneficial to beneficial, but rather it is of the type of adding what is not beneficial, indeed harmful, to beneficial. Do you not see that in fever, for example, a certain amount of medicine is sought to resist the heat that prevails in such a condition, and if an additional amount is added to the required amount, then this additional amount does not work the work of the required amount of repelling heat, but rather establishes a coldness that removes health and balance. The fourth aspect: It necessarily follows from what they have held that causing the death of the prophets and guides after a time of their lives, while leaving Iblis and his descendants among the misguided misleaders until the Day of Judgment, is most beneficial (aslah) in your view for the servants of God. Enough of this as an atrocity. The fifth aspect: It necessarily follows from their doctrine that God Almighty did not do what was obligatory upon Him with everyone who lived soundly until he reached maturity and disbelieved or apostatized after Islam, because causing him to die as a child or depriving him of his intellect would have been most beneficial for him, but He did not do it. If you claim that the most beneficial is the obligation and exposure to eternal bliss because that is the higher of the two stations, and He has done this to those you mentioned, we say: Then He has not done what is most beneficial to everyone whom He caused to die as a child or inflicted with insanity, because He did not keep any of these until they reached maturity soundly so as to expose them to the higher of the two stations. If it is said: He knew among these that if any of them lived, he would go astray and lead others astray, so He caused him to die for his benefit and the benefit of others. We say: So why did He not cause Pharaoh, Haman, Mazdak, Zardasht, and others among the misguided misleaders to die as children? And this aspect is the core of the debate that took place between Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Al-Ash'ari was one of al-Jubba'i's students, and the teacher (al-Jubba'i) was one day expounding this issue in his lesson. So Abu al-Hasan said: What do you say about three brothers: one died as an adult obedient, the second died as an adult disobedient, and the third died as a child? Al-Jubba'i said: The first is rewarded with Paradise, the second is punished with Hellfire, and the third is neither rewarded nor punished (that according to their doctrine of the station between the two stations). Al-Ash'ari said: If the third says: O Lord, why did You cause me to die as a child and not keep me until I grew up so that I would obey You and enter Paradise? Al-Jubba'i said: His Lord says to him: I knew that if you grew up you would disobey and enter Hellfire, so the most beneficial for you was that you die as a child. Al-Ash'ari said: If the second says: O Lord, since You knew that if I grew up I would disobey and enter Hellfire, why did You not cause me to die as a child so that I would be like my brother? What does the Lord say? Al-Jubba'i was dumbfounded. [؟] And from that time, al-Ash'ari left his (al-Jubba'i's) lessons and doctrine, and he and his followers occupied themselves with refuting the doctrine
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive refutation of the Mu'tazili principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-aslah) for His creatures. The author presents five distinct arguments (wujuh) against this doctrine, preceded by an anecdote that illustrates the relativity of worldly states. The anecdote: A Jew confronts a Hanbali scholar (likely Ibn al-Jawzi) with the hadith that the world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever, pointing out the scholar's comfort versus his own misery. The scholar replies that relative to the Hereafter, the believer's state is like a prison and the disbeliever's like a paradise. This sets up the idea that limited worldly evaluations do not determine divine obligation. The first argument: If doing the most beneficial were obligatory on God, then He would not deserve thanks for it, since one is not thanked for fulfilling an obligation. But God commands gratitude, implying His acts are favors, not duties. The second argument: God's power is infinite; if the most beneficial were limited, an increase would be possible, contradicting its being the most. If unlimited, the obligation is unknowable. An objection likens this to medicine where excess harms. The author rebuts that divine benefits do not behave like material substances; adding benefit to benefit never becomes corruption. The third argument: The Mu'tazili view leads to the absurdity that killing prophets while leaving Iblis alive is more beneficial, which is plainly repugnant. The fourth argument: It also implies that God fails to do the most beneficial for those who reach maturity and disbelieve, since death in childhood would have been better. A counter-argument about foreknowledge of future evil is answered by pointing out that the same logic would require all tyrants to die as children. The passage culminates in the famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his teacher al-Jubba'i: three brothers—one obedient adult, one disobedient adult, one child. Al-Jubba'i's position leads to an inconsistency when the disobedient brother asks why God did not let him die as a child. Al-Jubba'i is silenced, and this impasse reportedly caused al-Ash'ari to abandon Mu'tazilism. The commentary follows the sequence: anecdote, then the five aspects in order, preserving the logical flow and the final story.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the medicine analogy rebuttal?
A) Medicine is always harmful in excess, so divine benefits must also be limited.
B) Adding benefit to benefit never causes corruption, unlike medicine which involves harmful elements.
C) Doctors are not good analogies for God.
D) The Mu'tazilites misunderstand medicine.

Key Takeaway
The infinite power of God makes it impossible to define a single 'most beneficial' act, because either a greater benefit is possible or the obligation is unknowable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power is infinite, can you ever assume that a particular blessing or trial in your life is the 'best' possible? How does this lesson challenge your tendency to judge God's choices by your limited measure? This week, when you face a disappointment, consciously remind yourself: 'God's power is infinite; no single act is the most beneficial, but every act from Him is pure benefit.'
?
You have believed that certain outcomes must be 'most beneficial' for you. But this lesson shows that because God's power is infinite, there is always a greater benefit possible. Does this realization humble your expectations and increase your trust in God's infinite wisdom, or does it disturb you? Why? Commit to reflecting on one instance where you felt God's choice was not optimal and ask yourself: 'Could it be that my limited understanding prevents me from seeing the greater benefit?'
?
The Mu'tazilite argued that adding benefit might cause harm, but the author says that with God, adding benefit to benefit never leads to corruption. When you experience 'more' in your life—more wealth, more trials, more blessings—do you trust that God's additions are purely beneficial, or do you doubt like the Mu'tazilite? Examine your heart. This week, when you receive an unexpected increase, say: 'I trust that this addition from God is pure benefit, even if I cannot see it.'

Divine Attributes

Third and Fourth Arguments: Absurd Consequences
Arguments showing absurd consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how the Mu'tazili principle leads to evidently false conclusions about who should be kept alive and who should die.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazili principle would require killing prophets and sparing tyrants—an absurdity.

The author now presents two quick arguments that show the Mu’tazili principle leads to morally repugnant consequences. If God must do what is most beneficial, then it would be more beneficial to kill prophets early (so they never sin) and to let Iblis live forever. But these consequences are unacceptable. The second part of this lesson extends the logic: if death in childhood is more beneficial, then God should have made all disbelievers die as children, but He did not. This inconsistency exposes the bankruptcy of the doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
Read the passage about killing prophets versus sparing Iblis. Notice how it uses the Mu'tazili logic to derive an absurd conclusion.
2
Read the fourth argument
Read the passage about those who reach maturity and disbelieve. Understand why the Mu'tazili would have to say God failed to do the most beneficial.
3
Consider the counter-argument
The Mu'tazili might reply that God knew they would be evil. The author counters: why not kill Pharaoh as a child? The logic is not applied consistently.
4
Synthesize the absurdity
Reflect on how these two arguments together show that the principle cannot be consistently applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقض قاعدة الصلاح والأصلح الاعتزالية
مَرَّ يوماً بالسُّوق في موكب عظيم وهَيَّاةٍ جَمِيلةٍ، فهجَمَ عليه يهودي وأثوابه مُلَطَّخةٌ بالدَّرَنِ، وهو في غاية الرَّثَاثة والبشاعة ، فقَبَضَ على لِجَامِ بغلته ، ثم قال له: يا شيخ الإسلام، أنت تزعم أن نبيكم قال: «الدنيا سجن المؤمن، وجنة الكافر»، فأي سجن هذا أنتَ فيه مع النعمة ؟ وأي جنَّة أنا فيها مع ما ترى ؟ فقال له الحافظ الله : أما أنا ، فإنَّ الذي أنا فيه بالنسبة لما أعده الله في الآخرة مِن النّعيم للمؤمنين يُعدُّ سجنا ، وأما أنت ، فإن الذي أنت فيه بالنسبة لما ينتظرك من العذاب الأليم يُعَدُّ جَنَّةٌ .
الوجه الثاني: لو كان فعل الأصلح واجبًا على الله لم يستوجب عليه شكرا، لكونه مؤدياً للواجب عليه ، كمَن يرد وديعة أودعها ، وكمن يؤدي دَيْنًا لَزِمَه ، مع أنه سبحانه قد طلب من عباده أن يشكروه على ما فعل معهم ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لِي وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٥٢ ] ، وقال : يُبَنِي إِسْرَاءِيلَ اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَتِيَ الَّتِي أَنْعَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَأَنَى فَضَّلْتُكُمْ عَلَى الْعَالَمِينَ) [البقرة: ٤٧ ] ، وقال : أَنِ اشْكُرْ لِي وَلِوَالِدَيْكَ ﴾ [لقمان: ١٤]، وما لا يحصى من الآيات .
والوجه الثالث: أن مَقدُورَات الله تعالى غير متناهية إلى حد ، وهذا الأصلح الذي أوجبوه عليه تعالى، إما أن يكون معلومَ المِقدار، أي: محدودًا بحدٍ لا يتجاوزه، وإما ألا يكون كذلك ، فإن كان معلوم المقدار محدوداً بحدٍ ينتهي إليه فإن الزيادة على هذا القدر أمر ممكن واقع تحت مقدوره سبحانه ، فلا يكون ما وصل إلى الحد المقدر هو الأصلح؛ لأنَّ الأكثر صلاحاً ممكن ، وإن لم يكن محدوداً بحد لا يتجاوزه، لزم الجهل بحقيقة الواجب. فإن قيل: نختار الأول ، ولا نسلم أنَّ الزِّيادة أصلح ؛ لأنه ربما يصير ضم المزيد مفسدة، كما ضم النافع إلى النافع قد مضرة ، ألا ترى أنَّ الطبيب يصف قَدْرًا مُعيَّنا من الدواء يكون فيه الشَّفاء ، فإذا أضيف قدرٌ آخرُ مِنْه كان مَضرَّةً ، فالجواب: أَنَّا لا تعقل أَنَّ ضَمَّ الصَّلاح إلى الصَّلاح يكون فساداً ، وقياس ذلك على الدواء والعلاج به قياس فاسد ؛ لأن الزيادة في الدواء ليس من باب ضم النافع إلى النَّافع ، بل هو من باب ضمّ غيرِ النَّافع ؛ بل الضار إلى النافع ، ألا ترى أنه يطلب في الحمى مثلا شراب قدرٍ معلوم من الدواء، يقاوم الحَرَارة الَّتِي تغلب في مثل هذه الحال، فإذا زيدَ على القَدْرِ المطلوب قَدْرٌ آخرُ فَإِنَّ هذا القَدْرَ الزَّائِدَ لا يعمل عمل القدر المطلوب من دفع الحرارة ، وإنما يثبت برودة تزيل الصحة والاعتدال .
الوجه الرابع : أنَّه يلزم على ما ذهبوا إليه أن تكون إماتة الأنبياء والمرشدين بعد حين من حياتهم مع تبقية إبليسَ وذُرِّياته من الضالين المُضلين إلى يوم الدين أصلح عندكم لعباد الله ، وكفى بهذا فظاعة.
الوجه الخامس : أنه يلزم على مذهبهم أن الله تعالى لم يفعل ما وجب عليه مع كلِّ مِمَّن عاش سليما حتى بلغ وكفر أو او ارتد بعد الإسلام، لأنَّ إماتته في حال الصبي أو سَلْبَ عقله كان أصلح له، ولم يفعله ، فإن زعمتم أنَّ الأصلح هو التكليف والتعريض للنعيم المقيم لكون ذلك أعلى المَنْزِلَتَيْنِ، وقد فعله هؤلاء الذين ذكرتم، قلنا: فلا يكون قد فعل ما هو الأصلح بكلِّ مَن أماته في حال الصبى أو أورثه الجنونَ ؛ لأنَّه لم يبق واحدا من هؤلاء حتى يبلغ سليما فيعرضه لأعلى المنزلتين. فإن قيل : عَلِم مِن هؤلاء أنَّ واحدا منهم لو عاش لضلّ وأَضَلَّ غيره فأماته لمصلحته ومصلحة غيره ، قلنا : فلِمَ لم يُمِتْ «فِرعَوْنَ» و«هامان» «ومَزْدَكَ» وزَرَادِشْتَ» وغيرهم مِن الضَّالِّين والمضلين أطفالاً ؛ وهذا الوجه هو لباب المناقشة التي دارت بين أبي هاشم الجُبَّائي وأبي الحسن الأشعري ، وكان الأشعري أحد تلامذة الجبائي ، وكان الشيخ يُقرِّرُ في درسه يوما هذه المسألة ، فقال أبو الحسن: ما تقول في ثلاثة إخوة مات أحدهم كبيرًا طائعاً ، ومات الثاني كبيرًا عاصياً ، ومات الثالث صغيرًا ؟ فقال الجبائي : الأول يُثاب بالجنة ، والثاني يُثاب بالنار ، والثالث لا يثاب ولا يعاقب ؛ (وذلك على قولهم بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين). فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثالث : يا ربِّ ، لأيِّ شَيْءٍ أَمَتَنِي صغيرًا ولم تُبقنِي حتى أبلغ فأطيعك فأدخل الجنَّةَ ؟
فقال الجبائي: يقول له ربُّه: علمتُ أنك لو كبرت عصيت فتدخل النَّار، فكانَ الأصلح لك أن تموت صغيرًا. فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثَّاني: يا ربِّ لَمَّا عَلِمْتَ أَنِّي إنْ كبرتُ عصيتُ فدخلتُ النَّارَ ، فلِمَ لم تمتني صغيرًا حَتَّى أكون كأخي ؟ ماذا يقول الرَّبُّ ؟ فَبُهِتَ الجبائي . تُمِثْنِي ومن ذلك الحين ترك الأشعري دروسه ومذهبه واشتغل هو وأتباعه بإبطال مذهب
Refutation of the Mu'tazili principle of al-salah (what is beneficial) and al-aslah (what is most beneficial). He passed one day through the market in a great procession and beautiful commotion, then a Jew rushed upon him with his garments soiled with filth, and he was in extreme shabbiness and ugliness. He grabbed the bridle of his mule and said to him: O Shaykh al-Islam, you claim that your Prophet said: 'The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever.' So what prison is this that you are in with the blessing? And what paradise am I in with what you see? So al-Hafiz [؟] said to him: As for me, what I am in, compared to what God has prepared in the Hereafter of bliss for the believers, is considered a prison. And as for you, what you are in, compared to what awaits you of painful punishment, is considered a paradise. The second aspect: If doing what is most beneficial (al-aslah) were obligatory upon God, He would not deserve thanks for it, because He would be performing an obligation upon Him, like one who returns a deposit entrusted to him, and like one who pays a debt owed by him, whereas He, exalted, has asked His servants to thank Him for what He has done with them. God Almighty said: 'And be grateful to Me and do not deny Me' [2:152], and He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My favor which I bestowed upon you and that I preferred you over the worlds' [2:47], and He said: 'Be grateful to Me and to your parents' [31:14], and countless verses. The third aspect: The capabilities of God Almighty are infinite without limit. This most beneficial (al-aslah) which they have made obligatory upon Him, exalted, is either of known measure, i.e., limited by a limit it does not exceed, or it is not so. If it is of known measure, limited by a limit at which it ends, then an increase beyond this measure is a possible matter falling under His power, exalted, so what has reached the limit determined is not the most beneficial, because what is more beneficial is possible. And if it is not limited by a limit it does not exceed, ignorance of the reality of the obligatory necessarily follows. If it is said: We choose the first, and we do not concede that the increase is more beneficial, because perhaps adding more may cause corruption, just as adding beneficial to beneficial may be harmful. Do you not see that the physician prescribes a specific amount of medicine in which there is healing, and if he adds another amount from it, it causes harm? So the answer: We do not conceive that adding benefit to benefit is corruption, and analogizing that to medicine and treatment with it is a corrupt analogy, because the increase in medicine is not of the type of adding beneficial to beneficial, but rather it is of the type of adding what is not beneficial, indeed harmful, to beneficial. Do you not see that in fever, for example, a certain amount of medicine is sought to resist the heat that prevails in such a condition, and if an additional amount is added to the required amount, then this additional amount does not work the work of the required amount of repelling heat, but rather establishes a coldness that removes health and balance. The fourth aspect: It necessarily follows from what they have held that causing the death of the prophets and guides after a time of their lives, while leaving Iblis and his descendants among the misguided misleaders until the Day of Judgment, is most beneficial (aslah) in your view for the servants of God. Enough of this as an atrocity. The fifth aspect: It necessarily follows from their doctrine that God Almighty did not do what was obligatory upon Him with everyone who lived soundly until he reached maturity and disbelieved or apostatized after Islam, because causing him to die as a child or depriving him of his intellect would have been most beneficial for him, but He did not do it. If you claim that the most beneficial is the obligation and exposure to eternal bliss because that is the higher of the two stations, and He has done this to those you mentioned, we say: Then He has not done what is most beneficial to everyone whom He caused to die as a child or inflicted with insanity, because He did not keep any of these until they reached maturity soundly so as to expose them to the higher of the two stations. If it is said: He knew among these that if any of them lived, he would go astray and lead others astray, so He caused him to die for his benefit and the benefit of others. We say: So why did He not cause Pharaoh, Haman, Mazdak, Zardasht, and others among the misguided misleaders to die as children? And this aspect is the core of the debate that took place between Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Al-Ash'ari was one of al-Jubba'i's students, and the teacher (al-Jubba'i) was one day expounding this issue in his lesson. So Abu al-Hasan said: What do you say about three brothers: one died as an adult obedient, the second died as an adult disobedient, and the third died as a child? Al-Jubba'i said: The first is rewarded with Paradise, the second is punished with Hellfire, and the third is neither rewarded nor punished (that according to their doctrine of the station between the two stations). Al-Ash'ari said: If the third says: O Lord, why did You cause me to die as a child and not keep me until I grew up so that I would obey You and enter Paradise? Al-Jubba'i said: His Lord says to him: I knew that if you grew up you would disobey and enter Hellfire, so the most beneficial for you was that you die as a child. Al-Ash'ari said: If the second says: O Lord, since You knew that if I grew up I would disobey and enter Hellfire, why did You not cause me to die as a child so that I would be like my brother? What does the Lord say? Al-Jubba'i was dumbfounded. [؟] And from that time, al-Ash'ari left his (al-Jubba'i's) lessons and doctrine, and he and his followers occupied themselves with refuting the doctrine
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive refutation of the Mu'tazili principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-aslah) for His creatures. The author presents five distinct arguments (wujuh) against this doctrine, preceded by an anecdote that illustrates the relativity of worldly states. The anecdote: A Jew confronts a Hanbali scholar (likely Ibn al-Jawzi) with the hadith that the world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever, pointing out the scholar's comfort versus his own misery. The scholar replies that relative to the Hereafter, the believer's state is like a prison and the disbeliever's like a paradise. This sets up the idea that limited worldly evaluations do not determine divine obligation. The first argument: If doing the most beneficial were obligatory on God, then He would not deserve thanks for it, since one is not thanked for fulfilling an obligation. But God commands gratitude, implying His acts are favors, not duties. The second argument: God's power is infinite; if the most beneficial were limited, an increase would be possible, contradicting its being the most. If unlimited, the obligation is unknowable. An objection likens this to medicine where excess harms. The author rebuts that divine benefits do not behave like material substances; adding benefit to benefit never becomes corruption. The third argument: The Mu'tazili view leads to the absurdity that killing prophets while leaving Iblis alive is more beneficial, which is plainly repugnant. The fourth argument: It also implies that God fails to do the most beneficial for those who reach maturity and disbelieve, since death in childhood would have been better. A counter-argument about foreknowledge of future evil is answered by pointing out that the same logic would require all tyrants to die as children. The passage culminates in the famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his teacher al-Jubba'i: three brothers—one obedient adult, one disobedient adult, one child. Al-Jubba'i's position leads to an inconsistency when the disobedient brother asks why God did not let him die as a child. Al-Jubba'i is silenced, and this impasse reportedly caused al-Ash'ari to abandon Mu'tazilism. The commentary follows the sequence: anecdote, then the five aspects in order, preserving the logical flow and the final story.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazili principle of al-aslah is consistent and leads to normal conclusions.
Correction: The principle leads to absurd conclusions like killing prophets and sparing Iblis, and inconsistency in childhood death.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth argument claim follows from the Mu'tazili principle?
A) That God must keep Iblis alive forever.
B) That it would be more beneficial to kill prophets early and spare Iblis.
C) That God should not create anyone who will sin.
D) That prophets should be punished.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili principle, when applied consistently, yields morally repugnant and logically inconsistent outcomes, proving it untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to trust that Allah's plan is best. But when you suffer, do you secretly believe a different outcome would have been better? This lesson shows how human reason cannot dictate what 'best' means for God. Will you surrender your definition of benefit to His?
?
If you had died as a child before any sin, you would have been saved from the risk of Hell. Do you truly thank Allah for the gift of life and obligation, or do you sometimes wish for an easier path? Ask yourself: am I grateful for the chance to worship, or do I resent the struggle?
?
The Mu'tazili error was imposing human logic on divine actions. Where in your life do you expect Allah to act according to your sense of fairness? Will you let go of that expectation and submit to His inscrutable wisdom, even when it seems 'absurd' to you?

The Three Brothers Debate: Crushing Blow
Famous three-brother debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the story of the three brothers exposed the internal inconsistency of the Mu'tazili position and led to al-Ash'ari's conversion.

Core Idea
The three brothers debate silenced the Mu'tazili master and changed Islamic theology forever.

This lesson presents the climax of the refutation: the legendary classroom exchange between Imam al-Ash'ari and his Mu'tazili teacher, Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i. Using a simple scenario of three brothers, al-Ash'ari trapped his teacher into a contradiction that he could not resolve. The story is not only a logical masterpiece but also marks the historical turning point when al-Ash'ari abandoned Mu'tazilism and founded the Ash'ari school.

Guided Path
1
Read the debate
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Identify the three brothers and their fates according to al-Jubba'i.
2
Understand al-Jubba'i's answer
Al-Jubba'i says the obedient adult goes to Paradise, the disobedient adult to Hell, and the child is neither rewarded nor punished (the 'station between the two stations').
3
Follow al-Ash'ari's first question
The child asks why he was not kept alive to obey and enter Paradise. Al-Jubba'i replies that God knew he would sin if he lived.
4
Follow al-Ash'ari's second question
The second brother then asks why God did not let him die as a child to avoid Hell. Al-Jubba'i is left speechless—he cannot consistently answer.
5
Reflect on the result
This impasse caused al-Ash'ari to leave Mu'tazilism. Understand why the argument is so powerful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقض قاعدة الصلاح والأصلح الاعتزالية
مَرَّ يوماً بالسُّوق في موكب عظيم وهَيَّاةٍ جَمِيلةٍ، فهجَمَ عليه يهودي وأثوابه مُلَطَّخةٌ بالدَّرَنِ، وهو في غاية الرَّثَاثة والبشاعة ، فقَبَضَ على لِجَامِ بغلته ، ثم قال له: يا شيخ الإسلام، أنت تزعم أن نبيكم قال: «الدنيا سجن المؤمن، وجنة الكافر»، فأي سجن هذا أنتَ فيه مع النعمة ؟ وأي جنَّة أنا فيها مع ما ترى ؟ فقال له الحافظ الله : أما أنا ، فإنَّ الذي أنا فيه بالنسبة لما أعده الله في الآخرة مِن النّعيم للمؤمنين يُعدُّ سجنا ، وأما أنت ، فإن الذي أنت فيه بالنسبة لما ينتظرك من العذاب الأليم يُعَدُّ جَنَّةٌ .
الوجه الثاني: لو كان فعل الأصلح واجبًا على الله لم يستوجب عليه شكرا، لكونه مؤدياً للواجب عليه ، كمَن يرد وديعة أودعها ، وكمن يؤدي دَيْنًا لَزِمَه ، مع أنه سبحانه قد طلب من عباده أن يشكروه على ما فعل معهم ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لِي وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٥٢ ] ، وقال : يُبَنِي إِسْرَاءِيلَ اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَتِيَ الَّتِي أَنْعَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَأَنَى فَضَّلْتُكُمْ عَلَى الْعَالَمِينَ) [البقرة: ٤٧ ] ، وقال : أَنِ اشْكُرْ لِي وَلِوَالِدَيْكَ ﴾ [لقمان: ١٤]، وما لا يحصى من الآيات .
والوجه الثالث: أن مَقدُورَات الله تعالى غير متناهية إلى حد ، وهذا الأصلح الذي أوجبوه عليه تعالى، إما أن يكون معلومَ المِقدار، أي: محدودًا بحدٍ لا يتجاوزه، وإما ألا يكون كذلك ، فإن كان معلوم المقدار محدوداً بحدٍ ينتهي إليه فإن الزيادة على هذا القدر أمر ممكن واقع تحت مقدوره سبحانه ، فلا يكون ما وصل إلى الحد المقدر هو الأصلح؛ لأنَّ الأكثر صلاحاً ممكن ، وإن لم يكن محدوداً بحد لا يتجاوزه، لزم الجهل بحقيقة الواجب. فإن قيل: نختار الأول ، ولا نسلم أنَّ الزِّيادة أصلح ؛ لأنه ربما يصير ضم المزيد مفسدة، كما ضم النافع إلى النافع قد مضرة ، ألا ترى أنَّ الطبيب يصف قَدْرًا مُعيَّنا من الدواء يكون فيه الشَّفاء ، فإذا أضيف قدرٌ آخرُ مِنْه كان مَضرَّةً ، فالجواب: أَنَّا لا تعقل أَنَّ ضَمَّ الصَّلاح إلى الصَّلاح يكون فساداً ، وقياس ذلك على الدواء والعلاج به قياس فاسد ؛ لأن الزيادة في الدواء ليس من باب ضم النافع إلى النَّافع ، بل هو من باب ضمّ غيرِ النَّافع ؛ بل الضار إلى النافع ، ألا ترى أنه يطلب في الحمى مثلا شراب قدرٍ معلوم من الدواء، يقاوم الحَرَارة الَّتِي تغلب في مثل هذه الحال، فإذا زيدَ على القَدْرِ المطلوب قَدْرٌ آخرُ فَإِنَّ هذا القَدْرَ الزَّائِدَ لا يعمل عمل القدر المطلوب من دفع الحرارة ، وإنما يثبت برودة تزيل الصحة والاعتدال .
الوجه الرابع : أنَّه يلزم على ما ذهبوا إليه أن تكون إماتة الأنبياء والمرشدين بعد حين من حياتهم مع تبقية إبليسَ وذُرِّياته من الضالين المُضلين إلى يوم الدين أصلح عندكم لعباد الله ، وكفى بهذا فظاعة.
الوجه الخامس : أنه يلزم على مذهبهم أن الله تعالى لم يفعل ما وجب عليه مع كلِّ مِمَّن عاش سليما حتى بلغ وكفر أو او ارتد بعد الإسلام، لأنَّ إماتته في حال الصبي أو سَلْبَ عقله كان أصلح له، ولم يفعله ، فإن زعمتم أنَّ الأصلح هو التكليف والتعريض للنعيم المقيم لكون ذلك أعلى المَنْزِلَتَيْنِ، وقد فعله هؤلاء الذين ذكرتم، قلنا: فلا يكون قد فعل ما هو الأصلح بكلِّ مَن أماته في حال الصبى أو أورثه الجنونَ ؛ لأنَّه لم يبق واحدا من هؤلاء حتى يبلغ سليما فيعرضه لأعلى المنزلتين. فإن قيل : عَلِم مِن هؤلاء أنَّ واحدا منهم لو عاش لضلّ وأَضَلَّ غيره فأماته لمصلحته ومصلحة غيره ، قلنا : فلِمَ لم يُمِتْ «فِرعَوْنَ» و«هامان» «ومَزْدَكَ» وزَرَادِشْتَ» وغيرهم مِن الضَّالِّين والمضلين أطفالاً ؛ وهذا الوجه هو لباب المناقشة التي دارت بين أبي هاشم الجُبَّائي وأبي الحسن الأشعري ، وكان الأشعري أحد تلامذة الجبائي ، وكان الشيخ يُقرِّرُ في درسه يوما هذه المسألة ، فقال أبو الحسن: ما تقول في ثلاثة إخوة مات أحدهم كبيرًا طائعاً ، ومات الثاني كبيرًا عاصياً ، ومات الثالث صغيرًا ؟ فقال الجبائي : الأول يُثاب بالجنة ، والثاني يُثاب بالنار ، والثالث لا يثاب ولا يعاقب ؛ (وذلك على قولهم بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين). فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثالث : يا ربِّ ، لأيِّ شَيْءٍ أَمَتَنِي صغيرًا ولم تُبقنِي حتى أبلغ فأطيعك فأدخل الجنَّةَ ؟
فقال الجبائي: يقول له ربُّه: علمتُ أنك لو كبرت عصيت فتدخل النَّار، فكانَ الأصلح لك أن تموت صغيرًا. فقال الأشعري: فإن قال الثَّاني: يا ربِّ لَمَّا عَلِمْتَ أَنِّي إنْ كبرتُ عصيتُ فدخلتُ النَّارَ ، فلِمَ لم تمتني صغيرًا حَتَّى أكون كأخي ؟ ماذا يقول الرَّبُّ ؟ فَبُهِتَ الجبائي . تُمِثْنِي ومن ذلك الحين ترك الأشعري دروسه ومذهبه واشتغل هو وأتباعه بإبطال مذهب
Refutation of the Mu'tazili principle of al-salah (what is beneficial) and al-aslah (what is most beneficial). He passed one day through the market in a great procession and beautiful commotion, then a Jew rushed upon him with his garments soiled with filth, and he was in extreme shabbiness and ugliness. He grabbed the bridle of his mule and said to him: O Shaykh al-Islam, you claim that your Prophet said: 'The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever.' So what prison is this that you are in with the blessing? And what paradise am I in with what you see? So al-Hafiz [؟] said to him: As for me, what I am in, compared to what God has prepared in the Hereafter of bliss for the believers, is considered a prison. And as for you, what you are in, compared to what awaits you of painful punishment, is considered a paradise. The second aspect: If doing what is most beneficial (al-aslah) were obligatory upon God, He would not deserve thanks for it, because He would be performing an obligation upon Him, like one who returns a deposit entrusted to him, and like one who pays a debt owed by him, whereas He, exalted, has asked His servants to thank Him for what He has done with them. God Almighty said: 'And be grateful to Me and do not deny Me' [2:152], and He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My favor which I bestowed upon you and that I preferred you over the worlds' [2:47], and He said: 'Be grateful to Me and to your parents' [31:14], and countless verses. The third aspect: The capabilities of God Almighty are infinite without limit. This most beneficial (al-aslah) which they have made obligatory upon Him, exalted, is either of known measure, i.e., limited by a limit it does not exceed, or it is not so. If it is of known measure, limited by a limit at which it ends, then an increase beyond this measure is a possible matter falling under His power, exalted, so what has reached the limit determined is not the most beneficial, because what is more beneficial is possible. And if it is not limited by a limit it does not exceed, ignorance of the reality of the obligatory necessarily follows. If it is said: We choose the first, and we do not concede that the increase is more beneficial, because perhaps adding more may cause corruption, just as adding beneficial to beneficial may be harmful. Do you not see that the physician prescribes a specific amount of medicine in which there is healing, and if he adds another amount from it, it causes harm? So the answer: We do not conceive that adding benefit to benefit is corruption, and analogizing that to medicine and treatment with it is a corrupt analogy, because the increase in medicine is not of the type of adding beneficial to beneficial, but rather it is of the type of adding what is not beneficial, indeed harmful, to beneficial. Do you not see that in fever, for example, a certain amount of medicine is sought to resist the heat that prevails in such a condition, and if an additional amount is added to the required amount, then this additional amount does not work the work of the required amount of repelling heat, but rather establishes a coldness that removes health and balance. The fourth aspect: It necessarily follows from what they have held that causing the death of the prophets and guides after a time of their lives, while leaving Iblis and his descendants among the misguided misleaders until the Day of Judgment, is most beneficial (aslah) in your view for the servants of God. Enough of this as an atrocity. The fifth aspect: It necessarily follows from their doctrine that God Almighty did not do what was obligatory upon Him with everyone who lived soundly until he reached maturity and disbelieved or apostatized after Islam, because causing him to die as a child or depriving him of his intellect would have been most beneficial for him, but He did not do it. If you claim that the most beneficial is the obligation and exposure to eternal bliss because that is the higher of the two stations, and He has done this to those you mentioned, we say: Then He has not done what is most beneficial to everyone whom He caused to die as a child or inflicted with insanity, because He did not keep any of these until they reached maturity soundly so as to expose them to the higher of the two stations. If it is said: He knew among these that if any of them lived, he would go astray and lead others astray, so He caused him to die for his benefit and the benefit of others. We say: So why did He not cause Pharaoh, Haman, Mazdak, Zardasht, and others among the misguided misleaders to die as children? And this aspect is the core of the debate that took place between Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Al-Ash'ari was one of al-Jubba'i's students, and the teacher (al-Jubba'i) was one day expounding this issue in his lesson. So Abu al-Hasan said: What do you say about three brothers: one died as an adult obedient, the second died as an adult disobedient, and the third died as a child? Al-Jubba'i said: The first is rewarded with Paradise, the second is punished with Hellfire, and the third is neither rewarded nor punished (that according to their doctrine of the station between the two stations). Al-Ash'ari said: If the third says: O Lord, why did You cause me to die as a child and not keep me until I grew up so that I would obey You and enter Paradise? Al-Jubba'i said: His Lord says to him: I knew that if you grew up you would disobey and enter Hellfire, so the most beneficial for you was that you die as a child. Al-Ash'ari said: If the second says: O Lord, since You knew that if I grew up I would disobey and enter Hellfire, why did You not cause me to die as a child so that I would be like my brother? What does the Lord say? Al-Jubba'i was dumbfounded. [؟] And from that time, al-Ash'ari left his (al-Jubba'i's) lessons and doctrine, and he and his followers occupied themselves with refuting the doctrine
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive refutation of the Mu'tazili principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-aslah) for His creatures. The author presents five distinct arguments (wujuh) against this doctrine, preceded by an anecdote that illustrates the relativity of worldly states. The anecdote: A Jew confronts a Hanbali scholar (likely Ibn al-Jawzi) with the hadith that the world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever, pointing out the scholar's comfort versus his own misery. The scholar replies that relative to the Hereafter, the believer's state is like a prison and the disbeliever's like a paradise. This sets up the idea that limited worldly evaluations do not determine divine obligation. The first argument: If doing the most beneficial were obligatory on God, then He would not deserve thanks for it, since one is not thanked for fulfilling an obligation. But God commands gratitude, implying His acts are favors, not duties. The second argument: God's power is infinite; if the most beneficial were limited, an increase would be possible, contradicting its being the most. If unlimited, the obligation is unknowable. An objection likens this to medicine where excess harms. The author rebuts that divine benefits do not behave like material substances; adding benefit to benefit never becomes corruption. The third argument: The Mu'tazili view leads to the absurdity that killing prophets while leaving Iblis alive is more beneficial, which is plainly repugnant. The fourth argument: It also implies that God fails to do the most beneficial for those who reach maturity and disbelieve, since death in childhood would have been better. A counter-argument about foreknowledge of future evil is answered by pointing out that the same logic would require all tyrants to die as children. The passage culminates in the famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his teacher al-Jubba'i: three brothers—one obedient adult, one disobedient adult, one child. Al-Jubba'i's position leads to an inconsistency when the disobedient brother asks why God did not let him die as a child. Al-Jubba'i is silenced, and this impasse reportedly caused al-Ash'ari to abandon Mu'tazilism. The commentary follows the sequence: anecdote, then the five aspects in order, preserving the logical flow and the final story.

Key Terms
المنزلة بين المنزلتين
التكليف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazili principle of al-aslah can consistently explain why some people die young and others live to sin.
Correction: The three brothers debate shows that the same reasoning would require everyone who will sin to die as children, which is not observed.

Checkpoint
Why was al-Jubba'i unable to answer al-Ash'ari's second question?
A) Because he did not know the future.
B) Because the same logic that justified the child's death would also justify killing the disobedient adult as a child, which was not done.
C) Because the question was about the afterlife, which is unknowable.
D) Because he changed his mind about the principle.

Key Takeaway
The three brothers debate revealed a fatal inconsistency in the Mu'tazili principle of al-aslah, leading to al-Ash'ari's rejection of his teacher's doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself reasoning about what is 'best' for you or others in a way that subtly places your own judgment above Allah's decree? What would it cost you to completely trust that Allah's knowledge is greater than yours, even when His wisdom is hidden from you?
?
The Mu'tazili teacher was silenced by a logical argument that seemed airtight. Is there a belief or assumption about Allah that you hold tightly because it makes logical sense to you, but which you have never subjected to the test of revelation? Are you willing to let a potential inconsistency in your own reasoning drive you to deeper submission to the divine text?
?
Al-Ash'ari abandoned the theology of his teacher because he saw the inconsistency. Think of one worldview or habit you inherited from someone you respect. What would it take for you to reject it publicly if you found it violated Allah's truth? Are you prepared to face the silence of your own 'al-Jubba'i'?
